Parliament Does Not Support Amendment Freeing Tymoshenko <EN>
Today , the Ukraine parliament dismissed , within the Code of Criminal Procedure amendment , the motion to revoke an article based on which the opposition leader , Yulia Tymoshenko , was sentenced . <EN>
The amendment that would lead to freeing the imprisoned former Prime Minister was revoked during second reading of the proposal for mitigation of sentences for economic offences . <EN>
In October , Tymoshenko was sentenced to seven years in prison for entering into what was reported to be a disadvantageous gas deal with Russia . <EN>
The verdict is not yet final; the court will hear Tymoshenko &apos;s appeal in December . <EN>
Tymoshenko claims the verdict is a political revenge of the regime; in the West , the trial has also evoked suspicion of being biased . <EN>
The proposal to remove Article 365 from the Code of Criminal Procedure , upon which the former Prime Minister was sentenced , was supported by 147 members of parliament . <EN>
Its ratification would require 226 votes . <EN>
Libya &apos;s Victory <EN>
The story of Libya &apos;s liberation , or rebellion , already has its defeated . <EN>
Muammar Kaddafi is buried at an unknown place in the desert . Without him , the war is over . <EN>
It is time to define the winners . <EN>
As a rule , Islamists win in the country; the question is whether they are the moderate or the radical ones . <EN>
The transitional cabinet declared itself a follower of the customary Sharia law , of which we have already heard . <EN>
Libya will become a crime free country , as the punishment for stealing is having one &apos;s hand amputated . <EN>
Women can forget about emancipation; potential religious renegades will be executed; etc . <EN>
Instead of a dictator , a society consisting of competing tribes will be united by Koran . <EN>
Libya will be in an order we cannot imagine and surely would not ask for . <EN>
However , our lifestyle is neither unique nor the best one and would not , most probably , be suitable for , for example , the people of Libya . <EN>
In fact , it is a wonder that the Islamic fighters accepted help from the nonbelievers . <EN>
Their only excuse is that from their point of view , NATO raids were not controlled by an American general , but Allah , the greatness of whom they celebrated with each strike . <EN>
When winners are sought for in Libya , the West is not on the list . <EN>
We participated in a shooting , served Islam , and our politicians got rid of a dictator , their political ally , without any guarantee of profit . <EN>
Given the recent bad experience from Afghanistan and Iraq , we decided against military occupation of Libya . <EN>
The locals thus do not have to worry about expelling of the &quot; crusaders . &quot; <EN>
Without the occupation , will the oil companies get Libya &apos;s black gold for next to nothing , though ? <EN>
It is quite likely that they will not . The West will then finally be able to boast about its selfless protection of human rights . <EN>
Unless the followers of the Sharia law put a stop to that . <EN>
New Era of Crisis Commences <EN>
France and the rest of Europe are now in the investors &quot; spotlight . <EN>
A statistical storm blew over Europe on Tuesday . <EN>
Individual countries released their 3Q GDP data . <EN>
Between quarters , the Czech economy stagnated; Germany and France are growing . <EN>
Yet the debit market is breaking records today . <EN>
Investors are no longer looking at only Italy; they now focus on Spain , France , Austria , and others . <EN>
Eurozone statistical offices in Germany , Czech Republic , and some other countries , released their preliminary estimates of economic development in the third quarter . <EN>
Germany &apos;s GDP has grown by the expected 0.5%; and France &apos;s by 0.4% . <EN>
Both countries also adjusted their second quarter data , where Germany did better than expected (a 0.3% increase instead of the original 0.1%). France reported a slight decrease , by 0.1% (the original information suggested stagnation). <EN>
In this year &apos;s third quarter , the Czech economy showed an interim increase of 1.5% . <EN>
Between the quarters though , the GDP stagnated . According to the Czech Statistical Office , this confirmed the trend of a gradual slowing of economic growth . <EN>
The results are worse than estimates by analysts . <EN>
Key events: <EN>
In this year &apos;s third quarter , Czech economy showed an interim increase of 1.5%; however , it stagnated between the quarters . <EN>
Based on preliminary and seasonal data , in the third quarter , the German economy grew by 0.5% . <EN>
Between July and September , the economy of both the Eurozone and the European Union grew , compared to the previous quarter , by 0.2% , which corresponds with estimates by analysts . <EN>
The Greek economy showed an interim decrease of 5.2% . <EN>
The earnings on its 10-year bonds are 28.45% . <EN>
Earnings of both Italian and Spanish bonds are growing towards critical limits . <EN>
Even Austria , Netherlands , France , and Belgium , etc. are beginning to experience problems . <EN>
Despite the fact that the situation in the region is getting worse , earnings of Czech 1 - year bonds stay under 4% . <EN>
Voices are coming from Germany , suggesting that ECB be the last resort creditor . <EN>
Czechs qualified for EURO . <EN>
In Montenegro they won 1: 0 and celebrate a 200 million windfall . <EN>
Football representation successfully managed the toughest task of the season ! <EN>
Thanks to both the great Čech and beautiful goal of Petr Jiráček , they won 1: 0 . <EN>
In the second half , Czech football was lucky to maintain its luxury lead from the home return match , and will again feature at the European Championship . <EN>
IHNED.cz watched the progress match in a detailed report . <EN>
Nearly no excitement in the first half , and a great portion of luck in the other . <EN>
Czech representation team , partially due to the home team &apos;s failure in the close; the great Čech; and heroic Jiráček; won 1: 0 in Montenegro , and celebrates moving on to the European Championship . <EN>
Perfect Czech team defence only allowed the Montenegro team to threaten in the second half . <EN>
Damjanovic and Vucinic became the match &apos;s least lucky couple after losing two great opportunities . <EN>
The wonderful Petr Čech is one of the reasons the Czech representation team will not miss the next year &apos;s European Championship . And Czech football will thus gain nearly 200 million Czech Crowns . <EN>
From the opening minutes , the game was very pugnacious . <EN>
Both teams found it difficult to join in the combination; the game remained around the mid-field line most of the time . <EN>
That was also why there was no pressure from the home team in the first half . Long kicks behind the defence were neatly averted by the Czech defence . <EN>
Iranian Students Are Prepared to Die for Their Country &apos;s Nuclear Program <EN>
They created a live shield . <EN>
Several hundred university students created a live chain around the nuclear power plant in Iran . <EN>
The gesture is to express their support of their country &apos;s nuclear program against a possible Israel attack . <EN>
At Tuesday noon , students &apos; prayers in front of the building were followed by their chanting of death to both the USA and Israel . <EN>
In Isfahan , Iran , several hundred university students created a live chain around Isfahan Uranium Conversion Facility . <EN>
This way , they express their readiness to protect their country &apos;s nuclear program with their own lives . <EN>
In its recent report , the International Atomic Energy Agency (IAEA) stated that everything leads to the conclusion that Iran has not stopped striving for a nuclear weapon . <EN>
Possible attack on Iran nuclear facilities has been discussed in Israel . <EN>
At Tuesday noon , students &apos; prayers in front of the entrance into Isfahan Uranium Conversion Facility were followed by their chanting of death to both the USA and Israel . <EN>
In case of an attack , aimed at the highest possible paralysation of the Iranian nuclear program , the targets would be , based on Israel press , the facilities in both Isfahan and Natanz , where the uranium is being enriched . <EN>
An Obese Child &apos;s Diet: No breakfast and sausage for dinner <EN>
Over a third of children between 9 and 13 are overweight; while 9% of schoolchildren are overweight , 5% are obese . <EN>
As a recent research shows , obese children usually come from families with unhealthy lifestyle . <EN>
Again , we can see the importance of the environment and models surrounding a human being for his or her healthy development . <EN>
For example , sausages occur up to half more frequently on the tables of obese children compared to the families of children with standard weight . <EN>
Over 19% of obese children had fried chips for dinner the day before the research connected to the educational event called Obesity is No Accident . <EN>
Moreover , the families of obese children do not practise sports . However , this concerns a majority of families of current schoolchildren - only 15% of the children said their parents find time for sports activities at least once a week . <EN>
The research was performed among 900 children . <EN>
The research took place at the end of last year &apos;s school year; it included almost 900 elementary school children from throughout Bohemia . <EN>
It was the second year of the Obesity is No Accident event supported by both Všeobecná zdravotní pojišťovna insurance company and Unilever . <EN>
So far , the project has been joined by over 12 thousand school children from 4th to 8th grades . <EN>
Proper diet and sufficient sports activities represent key defining factors causing dramatically growing number of children who are either overweight or obese . <EN>
&quot; For example , only half of those inquired said they have five meals a day , in the breakfast-snack-lunch-snack-dinner pattern , one of the basic preconditions of correct diet , &quot; one of the results of the research says . <EN>
No lunch and sausage in the evening <EN>
Experts warn that even relative details are crucial for healthy development; such as a regular time of family breakfast . <EN>
In the Czech Republic , only 23% of schoolchildren &apos;s families have breakfast together . <EN>
In a majority of families , everyone has breakfast separately . <EN>
The worst discovery was the fact that in one tenth of households people do not have breakfast at all . <EN>
Yet breakfast is the core of proper daily diet . <EN>
A survey has shown that fries are consumed more often in the families of obese children . <EN>
Nearly everyone - regardless of their weight - drinks sweet soft drinks every day (70%). <EN>
Though over 40% of children do sports regularly , the number drops down to less than a half - 15% - when it comes to their parents . <EN>
Compose your own menu <EN>
Another part of the survey allowed selected children (204 boys and 172 girls from 13 schools) to compose their own menu based on selection offered and their taste and opinions . <EN>
&quot; Diet preferences of Czech children between 12 and 15 are far from ideal as regards healthy diet . &quot; <EN>
Their favourite meals include large number of flour , meat , and sweet dishes . <EN>
&quot; Especially alarming is the high popularity of sweet soft drinks , &quot; the final report of the survey concludes . <EN>
As the main dish for lunch , pasta won very tightly over poultry . <EN>
However , children showed very little interest in legumes , fish , and vegetable lunches . <EN>
Tendency towards health <EN>
The survey also showed that children are willing to adjust their eating habits provided they are given correct information . <EN>
&quot; Many participants from the survey control group showed a significant shift of preferences towards healthy food when completing a questionnaire after the end of the Obesity is No Accident educational lecture , &quot; project results show . <EN>
This was quite significant , for example , in case of sweet soft drinks , where more children would begin to prefer plain water . <EN>
In addition , for their main course , children ticked poultry and fish more often , limiting sweet meals and dumplings . <EN>
A Stylist Must Also Be a Good Psychologist , Professionals Claim <EN>
In the opening article on stylist training , I was complaining a bit about the amount of information in the introductory lessons . <EN>
I had no idea what was coming . <EN>
Lectures by three experts from the field; dressing tips for difficult figures; and a seminar on how it works in practise . <EN>
And more is yet to come . <EN>
The closer we get to the final exam , the more information and practical tasks await . <EN>
The training takes place every Saturday and Sunday , but it is really packed with information . <EN>
This time , together with Alenka , the Director , (there is not a single man in the course) we discussed how to dress a woman whose body is not in perfect symmetry . <EN>
A majority of women are not perfectly symmetrical . <EN>
One has a short neck , the other has a boyish figure without proper curves , yet another is overweight . <EN>
A stylist must know how to optically soften wide shoulders , make the neck look longer , or add the curves necessary . <EN>
We were given tips on how to accentuate the figure of women such as Jennifer Lopez , i.e. with bigger breasts and hips and narrow waist , and not to dress them too provocatively . <EN>
For example , if the difference between the waist and hips is such that the skirt or trousers do not fit , it is worth to have at least one piece custom-made . <EN>
You will definitely not regret the investment , as perfectly fitting clothes are priceless . <EN>
In a custom-made skirt , you will feel much better than in one that keeps shifting , rolling up , sticking out in your waist , etc . <EN>
Boyish figures , on the other hand , can wear clothes with ruffling , appliqué , embroidery , or shirring . <EN>
Given the abundance of such information and figure types , I am glad to have a whole week to sort it all out in my head . <EN>
Still , I fear it is too much , with regard to the homework we were given . <EN>
Each of the course participants was given a celebrity to create two outfits for: day and night . <EN>
We must consider their current appearance , their fashion style , and figure type . <EN>
I am to dress Miranda Kerr whom you may know from the Victoria &apos;s Secret campaigns . <EN>
Inside I rejoice , as she is so much easier to dress than , say , Britney Spears , Christina Aguilera , who has recently gained about a ton (please , understand I am exaggerating), or the very young Selena Gomez . <EN>
We must cut the clothes out of magazines or find them on the Internet and print and graphically process them . <EN>
Moodboard , as the result is called , then expresses our personal style and attitude to graphic depiction . <EN>
It is important to think about the graphic part of styling . <EN>
A stylist does not just dress physical people , but creates product pages in magazines (based on specific instructions , for example , trendy purses , coats , etc .). <EN>
This is what a stylist and designer , Mario Kameník , was telling us about . <EN>
But that was not until Sunday . <EN>
A stylist needs general knowledge <EN>
Saturday &apos;s lecture , filled with information on figure types , was livened up by three guests from the field . <EN>
A stylist , Honza Pokorný; a fashion designer , Jakub Polanka; and a fashion photographer , Ben Renč . <EN>
Jakub reminded us that fashion is an illusion , and a stylist should be able to use this fact . <EN>
A good stylist can work with a single piece of clothing in different ways . <EN>
In this case , variability is key . <EN>
For example , a trench coat may be worn in the standard way , over jeans and T-shirt , as a coat; but it may also be worn on naked body , with step-ins , as a dress . <EN>
Another option is rolling up the sleeves or collar , and the entire look changes completely . <EN>
&quot; Play with it , &quot; he emphasised . <EN>
However , I appreciated the following advice the most: &quot; For your work , you need to know the rules perfectly . &quot; <EN>
&apos;Then you can start breaking them , &apos; Jakub told us . <EN>
Here I finally understood why we drill all the definitions and rules of what to combine with what and why , while in fashion magazines we often see something else . <EN>
Not to mention fashion shows . <EN>
From Ben , the photographer , I learned that a stylist must have more outfit versions prepared than the number he is to take pictures of . <EN>
So , for a ten-page fashion story (equals ten outfits), I have to be ready to create at least fifteen of them . <EN>
Now I also know that in the picture , a piece of clothing often looks and functions in combination with others completely different from reality . <EN>
We must therefore take that into consideration when creating an outfit . <EN>
Honza Pokorný confirmed that image and style often are half the success . <EN>
Just look at Madonna , who is no miraculous singer , yet her image and marketing turned her into a worldwide star . <EN>
The attitude towards stylist services is still rather cold in the Czech Republic . <EN>
Even famous people often consider it redundant (believing it is sufficient to be good at something , and how they look at it comes second). <EN>
And if someone finally lets us create their styling , then we should expect them to give us different (smaller) size than what they really wear . <EN>
Then , we are left to Google and find out if the tabloids wrote something about a celebrity gaining / losing weight , etc . <EN>
On Sunday , both Honza and Mario were stressing the fact that for a stylist it is not enough to know about fashion and be able to create an outfit . <EN>
Our work chiefly consists of communicating with people we dress; it is therefore important to be a good psychologist . <EN>
To be able to estimate people , not to pander , and stick to one &apos;s opinion . <EN>
&quot; If a manager asks you to go through her clothes and add some nice pieces , you cannot throw out her entire wardrobe telling her how awful the clothes are . &quot; <EN>
&quot; Find at least a few pieces you can praise , and recommend what to wear them with &quot; Mario says . <EN>
He also showed us what specifically a duty bag must contain . <EN>
That is the bag you fasten around your waist to carry all the props you need . <EN>
Aside from the obvious things , such as scissors , a sticky roller , or safety pins , it should have a nylon thread (for the stylist to use when taking pictures of products such as purses or hats), special clip-ons for holding the clothes in the back in case it is too large (pins and similar things are forbidden as they damage the clothes), or a sewing set . <EN>
To have some change from listening , and gain some practical experience , we learned how to properly underlay shoe soles . <EN>
Even when taking photographs in a studio where the surface is even , the soles might get damaged - not to mention shooting outside . <EN>
And so we were sticking away . <EN>
You must not touch the shoes with the scissors , to avoid any damage . <EN>
This requires real skill . <EN>
Mario pleased me by praising my job . <EN>
The skills mentioned are really not my cup of tea . <EN>
This is just a fragment of what we heard during the second weekend course session . <EN>
I am beginning to realise that to be a professional stylist is no piece of cake , no matter what people say . <EN>
V Need for Speed: The Run takes place across America . <EN>
Review <EN>
An originally carefree ride turned into a routine morning drive to work because of a series of completely superfluous and sloppy mistakes . <EN>
The ambitions were met to a certain point , but it does not matter since nobody obviously wanted to do any extra work . <EN>
Before it was released , the new version subtitled The Run created high expectations . <EN>
It promised to shift the old Need For Speed racing series in a new direction; the demos made it look like a game that might stand up in the action racing genre . <EN>
We were curious to see the sections where the main character gets out of the car and runs . <EN>
Typical for the NFS series though , in the end many things are different from what we expected . <EN>
The game represents a possibly decent arcade race , but the whole is burdened by several unnecessary mistakes featured in the series for a number of years . <EN>
This means they are not really mistakes , but the expression of an incomprehensible laziness of the developers . <EN>
The adventure opens very well . <EN>
You are introduced into a story , where the main character , Jack , decides to solve some personal issues by participating in an illegal race across America . <EN>
You get in the car on the west coast , in San Francisco , and your task is to be the first one to reach New York . <EN>
The idea brings several interesting features . <EN>
The route is divided into ten stages , subdivided into over fifty races . <EN>
This means each race takes place on a different route , and given stages are set in varied and interesting environments . <EN>
One thus does not feel the game keeps offering the same things . <EN>
Despite the graphics being on the same level of previous parts of the series , some of the environments are very nice to look at . <EN>
Still , it is nothing world-shattering . <EN>
Driving through the desert , autumnal countryside , or high in snow-covered mountains is visually very pleasant though . <EN>
In addition , the races are , from time to time , enlivened by an untypical feature . <EN>
For example , in the desert , you get into a sandstorm , significantly decreasing the visibility . <EN>
On the other hand , in the mountains , you have to be careful not to get under an avalanche . <EN>
Individual races are ordered fairly well . <EN>
There are just a few types , but it is sufficient . <EN>
For a while , you try to overtake a number of competitors (basically a regular race); then you try to beat the time (standard stopwatch race); or you are in a duel with a single rival . <EN>
On top of everything else you sometimes come across the police who make your efforts more difficult . <EN>
The parts outside the car are new . <EN>
They are just interactive animations , where most of the time Jack is running away from someone and you need to help him by pressing the right buttons at the right time . <EN>
Nothing difficult . <EN>
It is a surprise though , that these parts are much less in number than you would expect (just three to be precise). <EN>
It actually turns out to be good for the game , because this feature does not get to be boring; within what was already said , it is one of the things that make the game more entertaining . <EN>
The driving model follows the footsteps of the previous parts . <EN>
This means that it is nothing special anymore , but it cannot be considered a negative . <EN>
If you are looking for a real-to-life simulation , you will have to look elsewhere . <EN>
Still , this driving model is fully suitable for the action style racing , even though we could find better at the competition . <EN>
So far , everything is just right . <EN>
However , after some time , problems come . <EN>
In contrast with the driving model , the collision model is not that good . <EN>
From a game of this type , one does not expect complicated deformations and collisions , but when you have no idea , before crashing into any object , how your car will act , something is not right . <EN>
Typically , when overtaking or passing cars tightly in common traffic , you sometimes lightly touch the other car . Yet sometimes in nearly identical situation your car ends up in wild pirouettes . <EN>
Or , crashed completely . <EN>
This is not such a big deal due to the restart system , but is enough to spoil the fun . <EN>
The restarts are done so that if you crash or get far off the track , the game takes you back to the last interrupted point . <EN>
Nevertheless , there are only five restarts available per each race . <EN>
If you use them up , you have to start the race from the beginning . <EN>
This makes it an aid in case something does not work out , but you cannot rely on it completely . <EN>
Sometimes the restarts are not enough and you need to learn a given section of the race by heart . <EN>
A significant shortcoming of the game is the fact that the same things often happen in the same places . <EN>
For example , some turns have to be driven through in a specific way , otherwise you simply do not fit in . <EN>
At other times you meet civilian cars at a given place in the very same configuration , no matter if you come first , fifth , five seconds earlier , or one minute later . <EN>
This is especially annoying in situations where you can see how your rival drives through the two cars coming in the opposite direction so easily , while when you get there , the cars are already positioned so that you have to either drive around or slow down . <EN>
It makes no difference when you get to them; everything is set so that the situation always occurs just in front of your nose . <EN>
The competitors have other advantages , too . <EN>
While playing the game , you find several places , where , regardless of time , the same competitor overtakes you at the very same spot . <EN>
This is most obvious at the end of the game , on a long bridge , where you are driving in the opposite direction . <EN>
Obviously , your rival has to get in front of you no matter what . <EN>
The thing is that when he is driving in front of you , he makes your vision worse , which causes you to crash the car a few times in the section . <EN>
One can understand the attempt at making the game more interesting and adrenalin-filled , but it is so obvious it gets annoying quickly . <EN>
It &apos;s a pity , because despite the simple driving model , the game is entertaining and sometimes even so full of action you do not have time to pay attention to what is happening around you . <EN>
It is not important whether the reason you do not get bored is the concept with fifty unique tracks , ordering of races , or something else . <EN>
The idea of changing cars during races is unusual . <EN>
You have to watch out for gas stations along the way , as that is where you car may change despite the fact that in most of the cases the one you have is fully sufficient . <EN>
Cars are divided into three categories . <EN>
Sports cars are suitable for cities; strong American cars for straight highway sections; and exotic supersports cars for technical driving , such as along crooked mountain tracks . <EN>
The key story mode is closely connected with the challenge mode; these are the races in individual locations you know from the story . <EN>
Here , you gain both medals and experience points for your profile , common for both challenges and the story . <EN>
Various features unlock fir getting a higher driver level: starting with cars and ending with profile backgrounds . <EN>
Again , the profile is interconnected with an on-line Autolog function , which , among other things , compares the results you have reached with those of other players , and ensures community functions . <EN>
Yet another setback difficult to understand; is the situation from the last race in the story . <EN>
You and your car get into a subway tunnel (let &apos;s say you do), where you speed down the tracks in the darkness (let &apos;s say you do). <EN>
Your speedometer shows numbers from 150 to 200 km / h (let &apos;s say it does), when suddenly , a subway train comes running down from behind you , turning your car into a pile of scrap metal . <EN>
For several days , our editorial staff kept discussing whether when designing the game no one thought for a moment or whether its authors really think we are such morons . <EN>
The technical part of the game is nothing extraordinary; but the overall visual impression is mostly pleasant , sometimes even great . <EN>
It is a pity though , that in some dramatic moments , the recording , in some cases rather tragically , decreases . <EN>
This especially concerns accidents with large number of participants , where fluent recoding would not help you much anyway . <EN>
The sound is all right; the soundtrack is a matter of taste . <EN>
In order to please the widest possible young audience , the soundtrack is &apos; flecked in from all quarters &apos;; but there probably will not be many people buying the game because of its music . <EN>
Overall impression of Need for Speed: The Run is quite confused . <EN>
If the game avoided those clearly redundant mistakes , we could sincerely say that The Run is the best part of NFS for the past several years . <EN>
However , the game feels unfinished . <EN>
It surely is a nice entertainment , but prepare to be blinded by the mistakes with the strength of airport spotlights . <EN>
UK &apos;s Choirs Will Sing at the Students for Velvet Concert <EN>
The third year of the Festa Academia Festival offers joining the international Students &apos; Day and Velvet Revolution anniversary with a musical event . <EN>
It will introduce about twenty high school and university choirs . <EN>
The main focus of the festival is on two concerts taking place on November 17 . <EN>
&quot; Charles University has been greatly involved in the festival . &quot; <EN>
&quot; Participating choirs include the Choir of the Pedagogical Department and Humanities; Václav Hampl , the Rector , will be in the committee , &quot; Jakub Čaloun , head of the organisation team says . <EN>
The climax will be a free public concert by high school choirs , which takes place at 2 p.m. , on November 17 , at a plaza in front of the National Technical Library in Dejvice . <EN>
Celebration Jazz Mass , a piece by an important Czech jazzman , Karel Růžička is on the programme . <EN>
In the evening , in the ceremonial National House in Vinohrady , there will be a &quot; Students for Velvet &quot; concert , featuring university choirs , including those from the Charles University . <EN>
The aim of Festa Academica is to celebrate the international Students &quot; Day and commemorate the 22nd anniversary of the Velvet Revolution with dignity; as well as to present the public with top quality choir music , and to develop creative cooperation among young people . <EN>
The chief organiser is českých pěveckých sborů (Czech Choirs) in cooperation with Jan Kepler &apos;s Grammar School . <EN>
The entire event is under the auspices of Bohuslav Svoboda , Lord Mayor of Prague , and Václav Hampl , Rector of Charles University . <EN>
The festival takes place from November 16 to 20 , in Prague and Pardubice . <EN>
The programme offers both ceremonial concerts and numerous musical meetings , students &quot; happenings , matinées , and more . <EN>
For detailed information please visit festival web pages at: www.festaacademica.cz <EN>
EU Ambassadress Vicenová: <EN>
Czechs have the reputation of being negative and euro-sceptical <EN>
&quot; Lisbon Treaty caused significant imbalance between individual institutions . &quot; <EN>
&quot; I did not expect it to be such a tough war . &quot; <EN>
&quot; It will take five or six years before the situation becomes somewhat stable , calm , and before all players get used to their new roles , &quot; EU Ambassadress Milena Vicenová opened her lecture at the Law Department sharply . <EN>
She proved how true she is to her &quot; Clearly and openly about Europe &quot; motto in the very first part of her lecture , where she described individual EU organs and the relationships between them in such a clear and intelligible , way that many lecturers from the UK Law Dept. could be jealous . <EN>
Moreover , Vicenová praised the work of new long-term President of the European Council , Herman Van Rompuy: <EN>
&quot; At first , critics said he was plain , a grey office mouse who cannot fulfil any roles; I have to say everyone was amazed at how wonderfully he acquitted his role . &quot; <EN>
&quot; He is a person who can listen to all twenty-seven member states , communicate with them perfectly , and who has a clear vision of where the EU should be headed . &quot; <EN>
She explained her new position of foreign affairs and security policy representative as a reply to a question: &quot; Who is the European Union ? Which phone number should I call ? &quot;; i.e. as an important step to unification and better clarity of Union &apos;s policy towards countries such as China or India . <EN>
No One Wants To Ban Our Cheese Specialties <EN>
Vicenová further focused on the agenda crucial for the EU in the past , present , and near future . <EN>
She described Czech presidency from the year before last as a success . <EN>
Czechs were dealing with the coming financial crisis; they solved the as crisis; and organised the East Partnership Summit . <EN>
She said the fall of the government at the time was a great negative causing significant damage to the Czech Republic . <EN>
Currently , Czech representatives in the EU has been very busy . <EN>
As the ambassadress said , both the presidency and the following financial crisis caused an ongoing stirring . <EN>
In addition , a new seven-year EU budget needs to be passed , which is very complicated due to the current crisis . <EN>
Whether the budget will be slim and frugal; which fields will be given preference; which countries will be supported more and which less; all of that is on the coming agenda . <EN>
The ambassadress reminded the key slogans she took to Brussels: &quot; About Europe , Clearly . &quot; <EN>
&quot; I really do not like all the abbreviations , foreign words , and jargon no one understands . <EN>
How are citizens supposed to understand that in Brussels , people are not trying to come up with crooked or round cucumbers , different size bananas , or that someone wants to ban our cheese specialties.&apos; <EN>
She also wants to use the EU environment better , and get more Czechs into European institutions . <EN>
Multispeed Europe Is Coming <EN>
The ambassadress says Czechs are said to be Euro-sceptics; as well as people noticing the negative rather than the positive sides of things . <EN>
She wishes more Czech representatives were involved in European institutions . <EN>
She thinks numerous factors are to blame: for example , the modesty of our candidates and their inability to write motivation letters; together with low support from the Czech side . <EN>
Along with the success of Czech presidency , she highlighted the power and cooperation of the Visegrad Group . <EN>
&quot; Believe me that when I meet someone from Poland and Hungary , and a Slovak is coming to join us , the Frenchman next to me says: &quot; Hey , what &apos;s that gathering about , is that the Visegrad Group again ? &apos; and he is not happy about it in the slightest.&apos; <EN>
In the Union &apos;s future , Vicenová expects mainly new strict rules for the budget policy of member states . <EN>
Rather than a new European Federation , she finds the concept of two-speed , if not multi-speed Europe , very realistic . <EN>
&quot; We have both countries inside and outside the Eurozone . &quot; <EN>
&quot; We have Schengen area , and we already have an institute of reinforced cooperation . &quot; <EN>
&quot; For the first time it was said that the countries who want are to cooperate , while those who are not willing can stand off . &quot; <EN>
&quot; The number of such institutes will be growing; it will be a highly two-speed Europe , &quot; Vicenová expects . <EN>
In this regard , she appreciated the roles of both the Czech Republic and Herman Van Rompuy in pushing forward the rule based on which , all topics influencing the entire EU should be negotiated by all member states , and not just those belonging into the Eurozone . <EN>
Brand Story: <EN>
The IMB Innovator Starts the Second Century of Its Existence <EN>
Should someone search for the word that would best express the IMB strategy , the closest one would probably be &quot; long-term . &quot; <EN>
To the wide public , IMB is a symbol of technological revolution; the company is seen as a highly temporary one , yet it was founded over a hundred years ago . <EN>
The company &apos;s durability goes back to its first boss , a visionary , Thomas J. Watson Sr. <EN>
He believed in his motto saying that numerous world problems can be easily solved if people are willing to think . <EN>
His motto: &apos; Think ! &apos; thus become an imprint around which the life of the future giant would unfold (as well as the name of its internal magazine that IMB started to publish in 1935). <EN>
Moreover , it was the foundation of company culture Watson was building carefully . <EN>
&quot; For us in IMB , long-term thinking means continuous movement towards the future . <EN>
IMB survived and flourished for a hundred years , because it remained true to its original values , while it was not afraid to change everything around itself . <EN>
During our first century , this allowed us to transform the technology , business , and the company . <EN>
In the second century , we hope to be able to achieve even more , &quot; says current company Director , Samuel J. Palmisano , on the occasion of the anniversary . <EN>
Sophisticated System <EN>
In the 1930s , Watson approached employee care similarly to Baťa in the Czech Republic - people from IMB were among the first American employees to have a paid holiday , insurance from their employer , an elegant uniform , and a sophisticated system of bonuses for the best inventors and businessmen . <EN>
Just as sophisticated is IBM &apos;s long-term relationship with customers . <EN>
From the very beginning , the company was brilliant in exploiting talented people . It was one of the first world companies to abolish all discrimination , which rendered it with great selection . <EN>
Consistent with the anti-discrimination strategy is the current plan expecting a woman , Virginia Rometty , to take over after Palmisano next year . <EN>
She has been working in IMB for thirty years; she is currently a Director of Sales , Marketing , and Strategy . <EN>
In the last few years , IMB has been organising jams , on-line brainstorming sessions , from which many future strategies and innovations arise . <EN>
It is no surprise that the ideas are plentiful - the company employs nearly half a million people . <EN>
Institution with a Good Reputation <EN>
Company &apos;s strong business position is ensured by its strong internal and external image . <EN>
&quot; From the beginning , the concept of IBM was that of an institution rather than a technology company , &apos; a Harvard Business School Professor and author of a book about IBM , Rosabeth Moss Kanter , told the Economist . <EN>
&quot; IBM is not a technology firm; it is a company that helps to solve business problems using technology , &quot; George Colony of Forrester Research consultation company adds . <EN>
As the company itself says , there is a difference between entering a market and creating it . <EN>
During the hundred years , IMB , or the &quot; Big Blue , &quot; as it is called in the US because of its logo , has grown into one of the largest companies in the world . <EN>
It seems to be the most universal technology company - developing hardware and software; infrastructure; hosting; and consultation services within a range from servers to nanotechnologies . <EN>
It holds the most patents of all American technology companies; five of its employees were awarded the Nobel Price . <EN>
Its inventions include , for example , the cash point , pay card , financial swap , bar code , and floppy disc . <EN>
With about 220 billion dollars , based on market capitalisation , IBM has become the second largest technology company (Apple being number one) this year , overrunning Microsoft for the first time since 1996 . <EN>
View Ahead <EN>
Not all of its products fitted the taste of both the customers and period . For example , IBM failed with its own operating system OS / 2; Prodigy on-line services; and IBM PCjr computers . <EN>
&quot; If your business is defined by movement forward , you cannot be emotionally attached to the past , &apos; says Samuel J. Palmisano . <EN>
That is why IBM easily builds its foundations on many platforms - if they do not work , it leaves them . <EN>
This is how it differs from , for example , its competitor , Microsoft , which basically stands and falls on Windows , its operating system . <EN>
Perspective Technology <EN>
IBM &apos;s revenues chiefly consist of services , about one fifth for each comes from software and hardware . <EN>
While in 1990 , with over a half share , it was the strongest hardware representative . <EN>
Since 2000 , IBM has sold low profitable assets worth 15 billion dollars . During the same time , it has invested 58 billion dollars into purchasing of perspective technologies . <EN>
It has continued the investments even after 2008 , when the modern economic crisis first hit the world . <EN>
IBM follows the legacy of its first director , Thomas J. Watson , who increased the amount of investments during the Great Depression . <EN>
So far , IMB seems to be getting through the current crisis without any harm . <EN>
Since the beginning of 2008 , the price of IBM &apos;s shares has grown by remarkable 120 per cent; company &apos;s net earnings have been growing continuously . <EN>
IBM &apos;s company motto is to change everything , except for its values . <EN>
We may therefore expect that even if another crisis comes , this flexible giant will manage . <EN>
IBM History: From Cheese Cutter To Space Travel <EN>
IBM (International Business Machines) was founded in New York , a hundred years ago . Its original name &quot; Computing Tabulating Recording Corporation &quot; was quite complicated . <EN>
It took the name of IBM in 1924 . Originally , this was a brand used for company &apos;s branches in Canada and South America . <EN>
Foundations for the later IBM were laid by a merger of four companies , the history of which goes back to the 1880s . <EN>
They owned technologies such as the legendary &quot; time clock , &quot; i.e. a clock recording the time when employees arrive and leave work . <EN>
The architect of the new company was a businessman , Charles Ranlett Flint , who , until 1930 , also presided over the company &apos;s Board of Trustees . <EN>
Flint hired a director of a competing company , Thomas J. Watson , to help him with company management . <EN>
The leader then put the IBM &apos;s founder in the shade - Watson &apos;s ideas remain the base for invincible company culture and identity . <EN>
Watson led the company until 1952 . <EN>
IBM , as its name suggests , started by producing and selling various business machines - from meat and cheese cutters to cash registers . <EN>
During the first four years of Watson &apos;s leadership , the revenue doubled to nine million dollars , and company &apos;s vast expansion into all continents commenced . <EN>
Watson became so essential for the company , that after nearly forty years , his position in the director &apos;s chair was taken by his son , Thomas Watson Junior . <EN>
Under his leadership , IBM started to develop artificial intelligence and created the first programming language . <EN>
In 1960s , both people and computers from IBM helped NASA control space flights - to Mercury , Saturn , and in 1969 , man &apos;s flight to the Moon . <EN>
Meanwhile , in 1964 , IBM developed the first computer family - the IBM line System / 360 . <EN>
The classic PC that defined the computer standards of the period , called IBM 5150 , came to the market in 1981 . <EN>
Twenty years later , IBM sold computer production to a Chinese company , Lenovo , While buying the consultant division of PricewaterhouseCoopers , and thus commenced its full focus on consulting and high added value services . <EN>
In the past three years , IBM has been highly successful with its Smarter Planet concept . <EN>
Its goal is both smart exploitation of technologies in areas that have not yet been planned for and improving the situation in traffic or town management . <EN>
For commerce , IBM has recently introduced a Smarter Commerce platform that helps businessmen control the whole commerce cycle . <EN>
IBM &apos;s history is strong even in our country . <EN>
In former Czechoslovakia , as the first country in both Central and Eastern Europe , IBM founded its branch in 1932 . <EN>
Today , IBM CZ also runs a strategic outsourcing centre in Brno . <EN>
The headquarters for both Central and Eastern Europe resides in Prague , where there also is a world level research team focusing on voice recognition . <EN>

Iveto , keep the fool , I don &apos;t want him anymore ! <EN>
Darina Rychtářová (53) said it is over ! <EN>
After her husband , Josef Rychtář (53), became both the bodyguard and lover of Iveta Bartošová (45), Darina still hoped he would wake up and come back home . <EN>

&quot; Pepa may return home , but no longer as my partner , &quot; Rychtářová explained . <EN>
When Darina Rychtářová provided shelter for Bartošová in her house in summer , she probably had not the slightest idea of what was going to happen to her marriage . <EN>
Even though she had Iveta move out of Říčany 30 days later , Pepa would not leave the singer . <EN>
Moreover , he publically admitted he loved her . <EN>
After some time , Darina resigned , pretended to accept her husband &apos;s affair; and now she gave him her final goodbye . <EN>
Rychytář does not care who his wife sleeps with <EN>

&quot; We don &apos;t sleep together , and I don &apos;t care where she goes , with whom , and if she has a boyfriend . <EN>

When you ask men to name some typical bad habits women have , they usually come up with all of them in an instant . <EN>
Dear ladies , do you recognise yourself in the lines to follow , describing several women &apos;s habits that make the men see red ? <EN>

Development of Trip Prices Since 1989 <EN>
Until 1989 , only five state travel agencies were allowed in the former Czechoslovakia: Čedok , Sporturist , CKM , Rekrea , and Autoturist . <EN>
As travelling to the West was strictly limited , travel agencies of the time mostly sold tours to the socialist block countries . <EN>
For their holiday , Czech tourists thus went to the sea to the German Democratic Republic; Soviet Union (Sochi , Crimea near the Black Sea); Bulgaria; Romania (both to the Black Sea); and Hungary (Balaton). <EN>
The only exception was the period from 1962 to 1972 , when we had the opportunity to travel to Yugoslavia . Nevertheless , the Yugoslavian regime turned West , which caused significant limitations to trips to Yugoslavia for Czech tourists . <EN>
A great paradox of the socialistic period was that citizens of the socialist block (i.e. Czechoslovaks too) were not allowed free individual travel within the socialist countries . <EN>
If a Czechoslovak citizen wanted to travel , as an individual , to , for example , the Soviet Union or Poland , an invitation letter from the country was necessary; otherwise , individual travel was impossible . <EN>
At the time , travel agencies would offer some trips to the West , but one either had to stand in a line overnight , with a sleeping bag or have some &quot; good friends &quot; in the agency . <EN>
Still , that was not all . <EN>
A foreign currency assurance was essential for travels to the West . It was not granted to politically unreliable people , who were not allowed to travel at all . <EN>
Czechoslovakian currency was not freely convertible; without the currency assurance , it was not possible to obtain financial means (Western currency) for travelling West . <EN>
Most often , Czechs spent their holiday at home , which resulted in great number of cottages and summer houses , a habit that survives until now . <EN>
Since 1989 , Czech tourism thus experienced a real revolution . <EN>
While until 1989 , a holiday in the GDR or Bulgaria was the climax of our travels , last year , Czechs spent 4.5 million holidays in countries all over the world . <EN>
A great paradox we do not realise anymore is that until 1989 , we could not freely visit the currently most popular Croatia , as it was part of former Yugoslavia . <EN>
Right at the beginning of 1990 , visa requirements for neighbouring West European countries were cancelled . This started a huge wave of short-term visits of chiefly Vienna and Germany . <EN>
Czechoslovaks could not get enough of travelling to the West . Everyone wanted to go there for at least a moment . <EN>
For example , in Paris , Czech tours slept in parks in tents , because their income at the time was not enough to pay for a hotel or a pension . <EN>
A typical feature of Czech tourism then was bringing their own food (cans , salami , etc .) to save money . <EN>
Another important moment was the introduction of freely convertible Czech Crown . After decades , our tourists thus finally able to freely buy Western currencies . <EN>
Our living standards and average income were growing , which , around 1997 , resulted in another important moment . <EN>
Since 1997 , increased demand allowed travel agencies to prepare regular trips by charter airlines . Compared to the past , air trips thus became unbelievably cheap due to the ability to order quantity discounts . <EN>
By the end of 1990s , Czechs did not need visa for visiting nearly all developed world countries , except for the USA . This made our travelling even easier . <EN>
The next significant event in the history of after revolution travelling came in 2000 . High demand resulted in the historically first direct charter flight from the Czech Republic to an exotic country , Thailand . <EN>
Since then , direct charter flights take Czech tourists to warm exotic countries . This winter , flights from the Czech Republic will reach twelve exotic destinations . <EN>
Currently about 100 thousand Czechs visit exotic countries every year ! <EN>
Yet another important event of this period , symbolising our development after the revolution , came in 2008 . <EN>
On November 17 , 2008 , the USA removed visa requirements for Czech tourists . Our country has thus permanently joined the world &apos;s most developed countries . <EN>
For the first time in history , in 2008 Czechs spent more than a half of their holidays abroad (50.3%); and for the first time in history , they spent over 15 thousand Crowns per person per holiday abroad , including their costs at the destination . <EN>
General Meeting Should Find a President , Mate Threat Returns <EN>
For nearly five months , Czech football has had no President . There exists a risk that Ivan Hašek &apos;s successor , the head of Czech Republic &apos;s Football Association (FAČR) will not be known even after another extraordinary general meeting , which is to take place in Nymburk on Thursday . <EN>
There is still no agreement as to which election rules to follow . <EN>
Without it , voting for the three candidates will not start . <EN>
Jindřich Rajchl , Miroslav Pelta , and Tomáš Paclík are eager to lead Czech football . <EN>
Hašek resigned from his function in June . When leaving , he called to his colleagues to unite and find a strong personality who would lead football in the future . <EN>
However , Hašek &apos;s era sees football back in quarrels between both association chambers , unable to agree on a common candidate . <EN>
This was fully shown on September 16 , when a new President was to be chosen . <EN>
General meeting delegates wasted their trip to the National House in Prague , Smíchov , as the negotiations remained blocked , not just regarding the election method . <EN>
No agreement was reached as to who is entitled to vote at the general meeting - whether the statutory representatives only , or also officials given power of attorney . <EN>
This single point has been partially settled since , thanks to a recommendation of the Institute of State and Law , according to which representation based on power of attorney is not possible . <EN>
Arguments concerning the election rules continue , though . <EN>
The Executive Board has not been of much help either , though at its meetings , both regular and extraordinary , it is mostly preoccupied by this issue . <EN>
The view of election options has changed several times , but the key point remains the same . <EN>
The question is: How to proceed in the 3rd round to avoid mate ? <EN>
&quot; The argument is based on whether to follow the by-laws or to find another model , &quot; says one of the three FAČR Vice-Presidents , Dušan Svoboda , who represents professional football in the association &apos;s management . <EN>
Based on the model given by the by-laws , the winner of the 3rd round is a candidate with higher percentage support from the chamber he is the candidate for . <EN>
Moravia is said to accept a compromise to have a candidate with the highest percentage of total votes from both chambers win the election . <EN>
The Czech part stresses a condition that in the percentage total , the winner must gain at least two-third superiority . <EN>
&quot; However , the two previous rounds would then lose their meaning; that would completely deny the two-chamber concept , &quot; Svoboda agrees with Moravia &apos;s arguments . He says it would be best not to bend the rules and vote according to the existing regulations . <EN>
Somewhat surprisingly Tomáš Paclík agrees with his opinion even if it is estimated that the election rules defined by the by-laws fits Pelta best of the candidates . <EN>
&apos;I wish the elections follow the by-laws to the maximum.&apos; <EN>
&quot; I want to avoid all kinds of representative nonsense , as at the previous general meeting , &quot; says the owner of Viktorie Plzeň , who is a candidate for the first time; and in his statements he chiefly stood against Pelta . <EN>
Pelta remains an optimist . <EN>
He believes the new President will be known in Nymburk; he also hopes that in the future , the candidates will cooperate constructively . <EN>
&quot; All passionate stirring will calm down with today &apos;s prospective advance of the national team into the European Championship . &quot; <EN>
&quot; Football will be back on the happy wave , people will be more willing to cooperate , &quot; a Jablonec functionary says . Of the three candidates , he has the most experience with football management on both professional and regional levels . <EN>
Rajchl is more reserved . <EN>
&quot; I hope for an agreement , but the situation is very ambivalent . &quot; <EN>
&quot; It is not between people from Bohemia and Moravia , but there are attempts at purposeful adjustment of regulations . &quot; <EN>
&quot; That may cause another blockage of the general meeting . &quot; <EN>
&quot; I hope the common sense wins , &quot; Rajchl said . <EN>
There is not much time left for an agreement between the parties . <EN>
Some negotiations are said to have taken place directly in Montenegro; but who knows if the football generality will be complete before the match . <EN>
An extra flight that was to take , among others , the Vice Presidents Dalibor Kučera and Rajchl to Podgorica did not leave Prague in the morning due to a technical failure . An alternative was sought for in order to transport part of the executive board to the scene of the barraged rematch . <EN>
Finally , a meeting at ministry level , said to happen on Wednesday , may decide . <EN>
Minister of Education , Youth , and Sports , Josef Dobeš , would like to force the split parties inside the strongest sports association in the country to reach an agreement . <EN>
A lot is in the game: Government grants; football trustworthiness; and the planned ČSTV general meeting dealing with new direction of Czech sports following Sazka &apos;s financial problems . <EN>
Paclík Enters the Presidential Fight As He Cannot See a Suitable Candidate <EN>
If , before the extraordinary general meeting , the Head of Pilsen football players , Tomáš Paclík , saw a strong candidate , who would meet all of his expectations of a new Football Association of the Czech Republic (FAČR) President , he would not even apply for the top function . <EN>
&quot; If there was a good quality candidate , I &apos;d fight for him and not participate in the fight . &quot; <EN>
&quot; But no such person has currently been found , &quot; Paclík said to ČTK . <EN>
Paclík &apos;s motivation to join the fight with Miroslav Pelta and Jindřich Rajchl is to try to prevent Pelta , reportedly the favourite of the elections , from entering the top of the FAČR . <EN>
Moreover , Paclík emphasizes that should he win , he would only remain the President until 2013 , when a regular general meeting is scheduled . <EN>
In the future , he would like to see the position given to an experienced top manager , not excessively connected to football life . <EN>
&quot; I &apos;ve spoken to some people that could be considered . &quot; <EN>
&quot; I was terrible for me to hear some of them say that at this point , they don &apos;t even want to identify themselves with Czech football . &quot; <EN>
&quot; I &apos;d like to change this opinion , &quot; he said . <EN>
At the moment , Paclík &apos;s strongest disagreement with Pelta is based on the latter &apos;s connection to Roman Berbr , President of Pilsen &apos;s regional football association . Berber is a man of controversial reputation , who is , behind the scenes , known as powerful lobbyist , capable of influencing the votes of general meeting delegates . <EN>
Paclík therefore finds it unacceptable for Pelta to become the President . <EN>
&quot; If he wins , current situation will be preserved and nothing in football would move forward . &quot; <EN>
&quot; Combined with support from Berbr , a capable businessman , this would be even more harmful for the football , &quot; Paclík said . <EN>
He is hinting at the fact that some years ago , Pelta &apos;s name was recorded during phone tapping in a corruption affair investigation; Pelta came out without a sentence . <EN>
&quot; I don &apos;t know what prestige Pelta &apos;s victory would bring to football . &quot; <EN>
&quot; And how would we look in the eyes UEFA and FIFA , &quot; Paclík said . He is now more detached from his former statement saying he would &quot; sell the Pilsen club if Pelta became President . &quot; <EN>
In case Paclík wins on Thursday , he could imagine cooperation with Pelta in the future . <EN>
This opinion is shared by another candidate , Rajchl , whom Paclík supported before the September general meeting that ended as a fiasco . <EN>
&quot; He (Pelta) would be the first one I &apos;d go to . &quot; <EN>

&quot; I can see him as the head of the representation . &quot; <EN>
&apos;But he cannot manage the association.&apos; <EN>
&quot; I don &apos;t poke my nose in what I don &apos;t understand either , &apos; said Paclík , who gained a lot of attention in September , when he supported the removal of board of referees , led by Luděk Macela , replaced by Dagmar Damková . <EN>
Paclík claims he would dare to manage the association . <EN>
He refers to his skills from management of private companies; since last summer , he has been managing the Pilsen team that , with his support , celebrated its first league triumph in May . <EN>
&quot; I have the strength to make the football environment change , to support its improvement . &quot; <EN>
&quot; To limit the influence of some interest groups that tend to influence the disciplinary and appeal board , leading to disgusting situations , &quot; Paclík said . He does not hide his antipathy for , e.g. Sparta &apos;s Director , Daniel Křetínský . <EN>
One of his priorities would be the strengthening of relations between FAČR and the Czech Olympic Committee , with whose support he would lobby at the political top to get more money for sports from the lottery tax . <EN>
&quot; That &apos;s one of the key things the new President should attend to . &quot; <EN>
&quot; If taxes are imposed on gambling , as the political parties declare , I understand their arguments , but they must clearly say where the money will go , &quot; he said . <EN>
Paclík does not consider his connection with the Pilsen club a burden , though he claims that an FAČR President should be a non-party one . <EN>
Pelta is connected to Jablonec , and Rajchl to Prague Dukla . <EN>
&quot; It &apos;s not ideal . &quot; <EN>
&quot; Yet , I don &apos;t see a point in transferring my shares in the Pilsen club hypocritically to someone else , while coming back there in six months , &quot; Paclík says . <EN>
Pelta Promised New FAČR Regulations That Would Avoid Election Mate <EN>
Two days before the general meeting of the football association , one of the Presidential candidates , Miroslav Pelta , promised that if he is elected , he would strive for new FAČR regulations to avoid future disputes over the election rules . <EN>
Before the Thursday negotiations in Nymburk , a Jablonec functionary remains an optimist and believes that the pre-election fight would be significantly suppressed by today &apos;s prospective success of our football representation . <EN>
Prior to the failed election in September , Pelta promised that if he was to win , he would focus on both the representation and gaining of financial means . <EN>
He decided to participate in the elections before the last general meeting at the last moment . A two-month delay thus could have been useful for him to defend his ideas concerning football management in wider context . <EN>
&quot; People at all levels have been in football for long , and they expect the President to be known on Thursday . &quot; <EN>
&quot; They feel it &apos;s high time someone leads the association , &quot; claims the man chiefly connected with the Jablonec club; but he spent many years in Sparta and the association &apos;s executive board . <EN>
This gives him the reason to believe he is experienced enough to manage Czech football . <EN>
He believes current problems with elections are caused by the euphoria there was in the time of Ivan Hašek &apos;s reign . <EN>

He approached the rewriting of the key document of the civil association as a decoy for the delegates . <EN>
&quot; If I become President , I will take it as my personal task , and I &apos;m willing to take personal responsibility in case the attempt fails . &quot; <EN>

Other than that , he says he does not try to define himself against the rivals . <EN>
In the past , he has already announced he can imagine his cooperation with Jindřich Rajchl , whom he recognises for his legal education; he is well aware of the fact that his rival candidate should become his first Vice President . <EN>
For a long time , he did not attack Tomáš Paclík , who has constantly criticised Pelta . <EN>
&quot; He &apos;s been in football for over a year , and gained some success . &quot; <EN>
&quot; However , his attacks were not decent , and many people were caught by surprise by the method of his election campaign . &quot; <EN>
&quot; This is too , is why some of them now doubt his true character , &quot; Pelta said about his rival . Pelta himself claims to be true to the proclamations he announced in September . <EN>
He sees his strongest weapon in knowledge of football , from the lowest competitions to representation . <EN>
The representation should be the shopping window of football . <EN>
&quot; Í would also try to end all affairs , starting from the Bohemians case or the aftermath of last year &apos;s corruption scandal . &quot; <EN>
&quot; Right after that , I would focus on negotiations with both private and state sectors , to ensure enough money for the whole football , &quot; the forty-six year old candidate told ČTK two months ago . <EN>
He then promised that his arrival to the head of the football would not mean any personnel housecleaning . <EN>
&quot; I &apos;d need to learn about the job descriptions of individual employees . &quot; That was his message for Strahov , where the long period of interregnum causes understandable nervousness . <EN>
Despite current catastrophic scenarios accompanying the general meeting planned , he believes that on Thursday , the delegates will not come to Nymburk in vain . <EN>
&quot; If the only questionable point is how to perform the elections in the third round that is something we can get over . &quot; <EN>
&quot; Football needs trustworthiness it can only gain by finally having its leader , &quot; says Pelta , who , two days before the crucial day of his career of a functionary , remains an optimist . <EN>
Rajchl Promises That under Him , the FAČR Will Start Working Hard <EN>
If , on Thursday &apos;s general meeting , Jindřich Rajchl , the existing Vice President , is to become the President of Czech Football Association , many people in the Association would reportedly not be pleased . <EN>
Rajchl promises that if he is elected , hard work will come . <EN>
He wants to establish system changes and make members of the executive board responsible for individual football areas . <EN>
He also promised to solve the Bohemians case; improve relations with both UEFA and FIFA; bring more money to football; and continue the work of the previous President , Ivan Hašek . <EN>
