Europe &apos;s most beautiful pools <EN>
Leap into the water <EN>
By Julia Stanek <EN>
Paddling pools with universal fibre optics and status pools in Budapest . Travellers can experience Europe &apos;s incredible water - and relax tired limbs in a Jacuzzi after a city tour or a ramble . <EN>
One book can tell you where the water is at its best . <EN>
There was one thing Iris Meder could not do without on research trips over the last one and a half years: her swimming costume . <EN>
Lying back on the water , she has looked up at artistically designed domes , has swum towards marble cherubs awaiting her at the edge of the pool and has marvelled at meticulously restored art nouveau swimming pools . <EN>
She rushed to add any pool she liked to her notebook - with essential details on the construction and the history of the building . <EN>
The architectural historian Meder looked at more than 200 swimming pools - and has now compiled here experiences in her recently published book Badefreuden (The Joys of Bathing), covering everything from public swimming baths in Munich to historical bathing palaces in the Black Forest and &quot; hardcore concrete buildings &quot; in Taunus . <EN>
Her &quot; journey to the most unusual baths in Central Europe &quot; took here through 13 countries . Besides Germany , Austria and Switzerland , she visited baths in Italy , France , the Czech Republic , Slovakia , Slovenia , Hungary , Romania and Poland - and one city each in Luxembourg , Serbia and Croatia . <EN>
The 46-year-old is a real bathing culture enthusiast . <EN>
She has very little enthusiasm for sport , says Meder - but in the water , it &apos;s a different matter . <EN>
The only downside is that fans of swimming have to cope with blue glazed tiles and the stench of chlorine while joggers can breathe in the beguiling scent of spruce forests or listen to the bright twittering of birds in the park . <EN>
&quot; One day , I asked myself why swimming baths always have to be so ugly , &quot; says Vienna-based Meder . <EN>
&quot; So I started collecting beautiful baths . &quot; <EN>
Water surface doubles architecture <EN>
Splashing in the diving pool and ethereal sauna oils - the wellness factor in baths is so great because all the senses are stimulated , according to Meder . <EN>
And swimming baths can be a real treat for the eyes if the builders have gone to the trouble . &quot; You have the surface of the water in pools instead of a floor . &quot; <EN>
&quot; The surface is very transparent , but also reflects the beauty of the entire building . &quot; <EN>
Everything is mirrored visually: high ceilings , colourful tiles and diving boards . <EN>
The illustrated pocketbook The Joys of Bathing provides valuable information on the architectural and cultural history of historic pleasure and health oases over 190 pages - and makes you want to leap into the water . <EN>
Pool collector Meder discovered some notable examples during research in Hungary . <EN>
She found nitrate-rich water in a karst cave (the Cave Bath in Miskolctapolca) and a thermal bath filled with alkaline water in a bottle-shaped building (Városi Termálfürdö in Jászberény) in addition to magnificent therapeutic baths such as the 100-year-old Széchenyi baths in Budapest . <EN>
Many of the heated outdoor baths in Switzerland and Austria , on the other hand , offer spectacular views . You can view all of Zurich from a rooftop bath or look out on the snow-capped Arlberg from an outdoor pool in St. Anton . And there is a window in the steam bath giving a view of the action on the ski piste . <EN>
Perhaps the most unusual pool design awaits bathers in Längenfeld . The Aqua Dome in Ötztal looks like a UFO has just landed in the Alps . <EN>
It steams during the winter from three open-topped shells dwarfed by the Ötztal mountains behind it . <EN>
Alhambra in the Black Forest <EN>
Pool collector Meder was not greeted by the smell of chlorine in every swimming pool . <EN>
A lot of thermal baths smell of sulphur . The Árpád baths in Békescsaba , Hungary , smell so strongly of oil you may find it difficult to believe you are in a health spa . <EN>
The smell comes from the hydrogen carbonate in the alkaline water . The water is almost black with silt that sticks to the skin as soon as you slide into the pool - a wellness experience of a particular kind . <EN>
Iris Meder , however , was at one point disappointed in her search for beautiful bathing places . When she tried to visit the outdoor pool at the Czech baths of Luhatschowitz , she found the area sealed off . <EN>
The baths , designed by the architect Dušan Jurkovic in 1902 , have been closed . <EN>
When Meder looked through the weather-beaten windows of the red , white and yellow art nouveau building , she could see weeds growing up through the tiles . <EN>
One place where decay has been stopped in its tracks is a magical swimming bath in the Black Forest - the Palais Thermal in Bad Wildbad . <EN>
The baths have already gone through three stages of construction . You will not only discover neo-Romanesque elements from the period after it was built in 1844 , but also a Moorish hall in Alhambra style added around 1900 . <EN>
Following its careful modernisation in 1995 , the Palais Thermal is the favourite swimming pool of pool connoisseur Iris Meder - and not just because she comes from the Black Forest . <EN>
&quot; It is a real achievement to harmonise such different architectural styles so brilliantly , &quot; says Meder . <EN>
A dip in the thermal pool in such a palace is clearly of secondary importance . <EN>
Agricultural commodities speculation <EN>
Deutsche Bank has commodity trading investigated <EN>
By Christian Teevs <EN>
Will Deutsche Bank stop trading agricultural commodities ? <EN>
According to SPIEGEL ONLINE , Josef Ackermann has given a working group the task of investigating the consequences of speculation for the poor around the world . <EN>
The CEO plans to make changes in January . <EN>
Hamburg - <EN>
For German citizens the situation is clear . According to one study , 84 percent of Germans find it unacceptable that banks speculate on agricultural commodities such as wheat and maize . <EN>
Two thirds of those questioned demand that Deutsche Bank and other banks cease trading in agricultural commodities , as trading deepens the problems faced by the very poorest people around the world . <EN>
The findings were made in a survey conducted by the Forsa Institute for Social Research and Statistical Analysis on behalf of the consumer organisation Foodwatch . <EN>
The study is based on a report presented by Foodwatch in mid-October . <EN>
The author of the report , Harald Schumann , shows that betting on global commodities exchanges drives up prices - and the banks are therefore complicit in global hunger . <EN>
The campaign by consumer advocates is directed specifically at the head of Deutsche Bank , Josef Ackermann , although large banking houses such as Goldman Sachs and Morgan Stanley trade in the same way . <EN>
Originally , commodity betting was designed as a means of protecting traders against price fluctuations . <EN>
However , most experts now agree that the gamblers have left behind the rules of supply and demand - and are profiting at the expense of the poorest . <EN>
In contrast to US competitors , Ackermann has responded to the criticism . He has promised to investigate the accusations and has said that no trade is &quot; worth putting Deutsche Bank &apos;s good reputation at risk . &quot; <EN>
According to SPIEGEL ONLINE , an international working group is currently investigating the accusations contained in the Foodwatch report . <EN>
The investigation should be complete by the end of the year when the findings will be presented to Deutsche Bank &apos;s board of managing directors - with recommendations for action . <EN>
The head of the bank then plans to announce changes following the investigation at the end of January . <EN>
Commodities trading may be reduced or stopped completely . <EN>
Ackermann working on his image <EN>
The president of Foodwatch , Thilo Bode , welcomed the news while emphasising his criticism of the financial sector . &quot; Betting on rising food prices is an extreme example of how thoughtlessly banks are currently acting against the common interest . &quot; <EN>
As top bank lobbyist , Ackermann has a particular duty , according to Bode . <EN>
&quot; Deutsche Bank must remove all investments from its portfolio that bet money on food prices , &quot; said Bode . <EN>
&quot; It does not matter whether this is about starving people or the reputation of Deutsche Bank . &quot; <EN>
Ackermann &apos;s sensitive response is at first surprising , but then the CEO would like to present a perfect image just a few months before the end of his term in office . <EN>
Deutsche Bank announced on Monday that the chairman will not move to the supervisory board as had been planned . <EN>
Cancelling contentious food commodity speculation could improve his image . <EN>
He also need have little concern for the costs - it would be up to his successor to manage the outcome . <EN>
One in two people would withdraw commodities investments <EN>
Foodwatch is striving to keep up the pressure on the manager . <EN>
To date , more than 30,000 internet users have joined the organisation &apos;s campaign . <EN>
Bode published the survey on Tuesday . The survey was conducted for the Forsa Institute for Social Research and Statistical Analysis on 7 and 8 November and 1001 people took part . <EN>
No more than eleven percent think it is legitimate for Deutsche Bank to offer investments that bet on the price of foodstuffs . <EN>
Many banking customers would also take direct action if they discover that their bank is involved in such trading . According to the survey , one in two would withdraw investments that end up in commodities speculation . <EN>
43 percent would recommend leaving the bank , 49 percent said they would think about closing their account and switching to a different bank . <EN>
21er Haus in Vienna <EN>
The relocated pavilion <EN>
By Ingeborg Wiensowski <EN>
An architectural history with highs , lows and a happy-ever-after . Austria &apos;s Pavilion for the 1958 World &apos;s Fair in Brussels won prizes , became a museum in Vienna , stood empty and was abandoned . <EN>
Now it is being reopened as an exhibition centre . <EN>
Austria &apos;s pavilion , designed by Karl Schwanzer for the 1958 Brussels World &apos;s Fair , is a famous textbook example of modern post-war architecture with its clear shapes , glass halls , bold strokes and the new construction materials that expressed belief in technical progress . <EN>
Schwanzer &apos;s pavilion won the Grand Prix d &apos;Architecture in 1958 for its light floating steel-glass structure . <EN>
The building is considered a milestone in contemporary architecture . <EN>
It made the architect so famous that he also built Austria &apos;s pavilion at the next world &apos;s fair . <EN>
He finally shot to fame internationally in 1973 with his legendary four-cylinder BMW Tower and its bowl-shaped sister building . <EN>
The pavilion , planned as a temporary exhibition building , was relocated to the Schweizer Garten near Vienna &apos;s Südbahnhof , converted and opened as the Museum of the 20th Century in 1962 - and is widely referred to as the &quot; 20er Haus &quot; for this reason . <EN>
However , the building was not suitable as a museum for technical and spatial reasons - it had no walls to hang artworks and poor air conditioning . <EN>
Nonetheless , it continued to be used until contemporary art in Vienna was given a new home . <EN>
The building stood empty from 2001 and fell into a worse and worse state of repair . <EN>
The architect Adolf Krischanitz has now renovated the pavilion , which has been named the &quot; 21er Haus &quot; and will be used as a contemporary art museum . <EN>
The museum is a branch of the Belvedere museum , which will open the first exhibition on Tuesday evening - a delight in every respect . <EN>
Agnes Husslein-Arco who became the new director of the Austrian Galerie Belvedere in 2007 was instrumental in the new beginning . <EN>
Husslein-Arco , an art history graduate with a remarkable career in her youth as an ice skater , who went on to Sotheby &apos;s , the Guggenheim Museum and to become the founding director of the Museum der Moderne in Salzburg , convinced politicians and conservators to go ahead with renovation , attracted public funding and private sponsorship and decided on the use of the building . <EN>
The new museum was to house the Fritz Wotruba Foundation &apos;s permanent collection , a café and a bookshop alongside contemporary art . An office building was also to be built . <EN>
Strict supervision &amp; limited budget <EN>
Krischanitz was then the ideal choice to carry out the project . <EN>
He was known , of course , for having renovated and expanded Joseph Olbrich &apos;s Secession in Vienna , and had won the competition , but he also studied under Schwanzer at the Vienna University of Technology and the pavilion was an &quot; exceptionally important place &quot; for him where had visited exhibitions &quot; almost every weekend . &quot; <EN>
He knew the original design and knew the issues the building was facing , a building that had already lost some of its grandeur and lightness when it was relocated to Vienna and converted . <EN>
The problems facing the latest alterations were much greater . The building was &quot; an energy guzzler , &quot; says Krischanitz . <EN>
The window profiles of the glass facade were replaced , fibreglass-reinforced safety glass was put in and the glass roof was replaced by high-grade safety glass . <EN>
Thermal bridge steel girders were strengthened or replaced and asbestos was removed from ceilings . <EN>
Two lower floors created space for the new use of the building , a sunken light well between the building and the street provides lighting , a bridge leads to the entrance - almost a new building , but still the delicate Schwanzer pavilion . <EN>
The original external doors have been retained and the building has been painted in the old red-brown colour of rust-proofing . <EN>
And the cinema hall is exactly as it used to be . <EN>
All this under the strict supervision of the monument authority and with a limited budget . <EN>
&quot; We often had to find a material that was good , cheap and met with the approval of the monument authority , &quot; says Krischanitz , pointing to the rough flooring in the basement . <EN>
The building has remained flexible and light despite the constraints , problems and conversions . <EN>
Krischanitz stated recently that the pavilion &quot; from Brussels &quot; had been tough - a typical &quot; drop in the city &quot; story . <EN>
Architecture like this is &quot; always in the wrong place &quot; and nonetheless wants to &quot; stimulate a real awareness . &quot; <EN>
The 21er Haus is very much in the right place , as there has been a stroke of luck in town planning . The completely redesigned &quot; main station quarter &quot; with offices and residential properties is developing around the Schweizer Garten . <EN>
There may also be a second stroke of luck . The 21er Haus may be bolstered by another Krischanitz building - the collector Francesca von Habsburg has purchased the Temporäre Kunsthalle Berlin and is reported to be negotiating with the city for a neighbouring location in the Schweizer Garten . <EN>
Deutsche Bahn plans winter crisis package into the millions <EN>
Deutsche Bahn has come up with a crisis plan to prevent train cancellations in the winter . <EN>
The number of employees is to double . <EN>
The costs will run into the millions . <EN>
According to a newspaper report , Deutsche Bahn will spend more than 70 million Euros more this year in the battle to prevent winter-time cancellations and delays . <EN>
Referring to an internal crisis plan at Deutsche Bahn , the Bild newspaper has reported that investment of around 300 million Euros in total is planned up to 2015 . <EN>
Investment is intended to improve the availability of locomotives and the rail network , even in the face of extreme weather conditions . <EN>
The number of internal and external employees involved in removing snow from rail facilities and platforms is to double to 16,000 . <EN>
The aim is to clear platforms of snow and ice by start of business and 90 percent of the critical points within four to five hours . <EN>
Rüdiger Grube , head of Deutsche Bahn , warned of train cancellations and delays this winter at a summit with government and industry two months ago . <EN>
Last winter , Deutsche Bahn had considerable difficulties in its passenger business , as it lacked reserves in the face of difficult weather conditions . <EN>
Numerous new regional trains have been waiting for years for approval from the Federal Railway Office . <EN>
There is also some delay in the delivery of ICE trains . <EN>
Deutsche Bahn has also been forced to have the axles of ICE trains checked significantly more frequently for many years , after an ICE train &apos;s axle broke in Cologne &apos;s main station . <EN>
Deutsche Bank pays multi-million pound fine in the USA <EN>
Fresh trouble is following hard on the heels of the uproar around Josef Ackermann , CEO of Deutsche Bank: Deutsche Bank faces a multi-million pound fine in the USA . <EN>
As if the problems at home were not already enough for Deutsche Bank , the industry giant &apos;s past in the USA is now also catching up with it . Frankfurt-based Deutsche Bank will pay 145 million dollars (106 million Euros) to settle disputes arising from the bankruptcy of five major credit unions during the financial crisis . <EN>
The issue centres on the sale of mortgage securities . <EN>
The National Credit Union Administration (NCUA), a financial market regulator , accuses a string of major banks of having used false promises to mislead credit unions into buying the financial products . <EN>
The value of the securities dropped dramatically during the financial crisis and brought down the credit unions . <EN>
&quot; We are happy to have resolved the issue without the parties going to court , &quot; said a Deutsche Bank spokesman in new York . <EN>
The bank did not admit culpability in the settlement . <EN>
The same is true of Citigroup , which agreed to pay 20.5 million dollars . <EN>
The NCUA chairman , Debbie Matz , welcomed the responsiveness of the two banks . <EN>
The National Credit Union Administration (NCUA) is responsible for the US credit unions and intervenes in bankruptcies to protect customer deposits . <EN>
The NCUA is fighting for compensation for losses that run into the billions . <EN>
The current settlements are the first of their kind . <EN>
The regulator had also approached other major banks and sued JPMorgan Chase , the Royal Bank of Scotland and Goldman Sachs in the summer . <EN>
The dubious mortgage securities are so-called mortgage-backed securities . <EN>
They are underpinned by home loans . <EN>
This sealed the fate of a number of financial companies when the US property bubble exploded in 2007 . <EN>
The US investment bank , Lehman Brothers , went belly up in September 2008 at the height of the financial crisis . <EN>
The banks battling against a strong wind in the USA several years later . <EN>
Investors and regulators have brought a vast number of claims for compensation or to punish misconduct . <EN>
The Federal Housing Finance Agency (FHFA) has been behind the largest wave of claims . <EN>
It accuses 18 major international banks of having taken in US lenders Fannie Mae and Freddie Mac on mortgage transactions valued at around 200 billion dollars . <EN>
Deutsche Bank also faces legal action by the FHFA covering multiple transactions with a total value of 14.2 billion dollars from 2005 to 2007 . <EN>
The regulator is demanding that the Frankfurt-based bank take responsibility for &quot; substantial losses , &quot; but has not yet specified the exact sum . <EN>
Deutsche Bank has rejected the claims as baseless and has declared its intention to fend off the claims . <EN>
Warren Buffett pumps 10 billion into IBM <EN>
Financial guru Buffett is investing heavily in the IT company , IBM . <EN>
Since March , he has bought up shares totalling more than ten billion dollars . <EN>
Until now , the major American investor , Warren Buffett , had always claimed not to invest in IT and computing companies , as it was difficult to forecast the long-term development . <EN>
However , IBM &apos;s annual reports changed his mind on investing in the industry . <EN>
According to Buffett , he should have realised much earlier that IBM primarily offers services and purchases computer systems for the IT departments of other companies . <EN>
Investment by Warren Buffett is considered a knighthood in the financial world . <EN>
The IT veteran IBM has now earned the title of &quot; Sir IBM . &quot; <EN>
Buffett revealed that he had purchased IBM shares totalling 10.7 billion dollars since March on the US business news broadcaster CNBC . <EN>
His investment holding company , Berkshire Hathaway , has become one of the largest shareholders in IBM with a 5.5 percent stake . <EN>
Buffett said that even IBM knew nothing of his involvement until recently . <EN>
He praised the management , which has managed to bring in profits even during the economic crisis . <EN>
&quot; They have done a great job , &quot; said Buffett , referring to the management strategy . <EN>
For a fairly long time , IBM has focused on lucrative IT services such as data centres . <EN>
The computer pioneer - now more than 100 years old - also provides software and consultancy services , as well as powerful business computers . <EN>
Buffett had avoided technology firms to date . <EN>
He claimed only to invest in companies whose business he understands <EN>
and invested in a freight railway , for example , a lubricant manufacturer and a machine manufacturer . <EN>
His holding company , Berkshire Hathaway , owns shares in a long list of major companies such as Coca-Cola and Munich Re (formerly Münchener Rück) alongside around 80 of its own subsidiaries . <EN>
The 81-year-old took over the small textile company Berkshire Hathaway in the 1960s and built it up , with clever investments , into one of the most valuable companies in the world . <EN>
His lifestyle , however , has remained humble , <EN>
making him a cult figure for countless investors around the world . <EN>
His almost infallible instinct for making money has earned him a nickname as the &quot; Oracle from Omaha . &quot; <EN>
The IBM share price rose by one percent before the markets opened following the announcement of Buffett &apos;s investment . <EN>
&quot; Big Blue , &quot; as IBM is also known , is worth more than 220 billion dollars on the stock exchange , making it one of the most valuable technology companies in the world alongside Apple and Microsoft . <EN>
Buffett , however , has said he is not planning to invest in Microsoft . <EN>
The founder , Bill Gates , is a close friend . <EN>
Imminent danger <EN>
Following the discovery of the &quot; Zwickau cell , &quot; Turkish media express doubt about the rule of law in Germany . <EN>
One newspaper speaks of a &quot; bloody ideology &quot; that is now resurfacing . <EN>
The murder of eight Turkish and one Greek businessman between 2000 and 2006 was the result of right-wing extremist ideology . <EN>
Fear and concern has been the reaction to this report in Turkey and within the German-Turkish community in Germany . <EN>
For many German Turks , the news brings back to life a long-dead spectre . There has been no comparable right-wing extremist violence against Turks since the arson attacks in Mölln in November 1992 and in Solingen in May 1993 . <EN>
There was never any question , however , that xenophobia does exist in Germany . <EN>
The right-wing extremist network that has now been discovered , however , is on a scale that has not yet been fully understood . <EN>
&quot; Is this a revival of the bloody ideology ? &quot; was the headline of the internet edition of the Turkish newspaper Haberturk . <EN>
The Sabah newspaper , on the other hand , points out that one of the perpetrators was a confidential informant for the intelligence services and expresses concern that the German authorities may be caught up in the right-wing extremist quagmire . <EN>
The Turkish Community of Germany (TGD) reacted calmly , remembering the victims of racial violence during a silent vigil in front of the Brandenburg Gate at the weekend . <EN>
Just two weeks earlier , the Turkish Community in Berlin had commemorated the fiftieth anniversary of the German-Turkish bilateral agreement on labour recruitment in a ceremony with German and Turkish politicians . <EN>
Cooperation between the two countries was presented in a positive light - as a success story . <EN>
The coverage by some Turkish media has been like a slap in the face . &quot; Germany &apos;s present on the fiftieth anniversary &quot; is the title of one article on the Haber X Turkish internet platform , which comments on the circumstances around the series of murders . <EN>
The German edition of Hürriyet also does not miss the chance to make this connection . <EN>
&quot; It is beginning to stink , &quot; is the title of the column by Ahmet Külahci . <EN>
He points out that people have been murdered who had paid taxes and made an important contribution to Germany &apos;s redevelopment with their work . <EN>
The behaviour of the police and the subsequently successful manhunt is heavily criticised on German-Turkish internet forums . <EN>
The authors are asking themselves why the German authorities did not think earlier to look for suspects in right-wing extremist circles . <EN>
Some writers even go as far as some strong rhetoric . &quot; If things continue to be done so cack-handedly , migrants have no option but armed self-defence . &quot; <EN>
&quot; That will be the best self-defence . &quot; <EN>
&quot; Peace in Germany depends very strongly on how the entire network is uncovered and on the appropriateness of punishment , &quot; writes &quot; Selen . &quot; <EN>
The attacks on Mölln and Solingen in the 90s are an example of what it means for peace in Germany to be at risk . <EN>
The photo of the burnt out ruin of Solingen is deeply engrained in German and Turkish memory . <EN>
No other event has shown the Turks living here more clearly that there is imminent danger and shown the Germans that mistrust and distance can culminate in real violence . <EN>
The attacks , however , increased the sense of Turkish unity . <EN>
Do not repeat the mistakes of the past <EN>
The Turkish press at the time complained mainly of the failure of German policy following the attacks . Helmut Kohl declined to visit the survivors in Mölln . <EN>
He sent a telegram of commiseration to the Turkish president after the arson attack in Solingen , but it was his foreign minister , Klaus Kinkel , who took his place at the memorial ceremony in Cologne - Kinkel summed up in his speech the taxes Turks contribute in Germany , <EN>
just as if he were calculating the value of a person by the taxes he pays . <EN>
The coverage by the Turkish media at the time again shows how deep the mistrust of many German Turks in the current German state has become since . <EN>
Straight talking is what is needed now , alongside efforts to identify and reassess right-wing extremist terrorism in Germany . <EN>
The Lake Zurich banking scandal <EN>
The most risk-taking bank in Europe is not in Italy or France , but in Switzerland . <EN>
UBS almost went bankrupt during the financial crisis and has been struggling from one crisis to the next ever since . <EN>
A German is now to bring it back in line . <EN>
Axel Weber certainly had not imagined that would be his role . <EN>
After his spectacular departure from the head of the Federal bank , it was announced in July that he would be starting an almost equally spectacular new job in 2013: Chairman of the Board of Directors of the major Swiss bank UBS - an unexpected and lucrative career move . <EN>
Axel Weber was clearly delighted , praising Switzerland for its beauty and UBS for its newly won solidity and making some friendly remarks about his future colleagues . <EN>
&quot; UBS has managed to turn around . &quot; <EN>
&quot; I am looking forward to working with Kaspar Villiger and Oswald Grübel . &quot; <EN>
But by September it was already clear that everything would be very different . <EN>
A UBS trader in London had bypassed all the bank &apos;s security systems and gambled away around 1.7 billion Euros . <EN>
UBS CEO , Oswald Grübel - a banker not only famous in Switzerland - had to go . <EN>
The UBS Chairman has been considered ailing ever since - and everyone is asking: when will Axel Weber finally arrive ? <EN>
Weber is to advise the bank from February 2012 . <EN>
And he will take on the role of Chairman of the Board in May , and not in 2013 , the bank announced on Tuesday . <EN>
That will be tough for Axel Weber . <EN>
He is an economics professor and central banker , not a conventional banker , and clearly would need some time to adjust . <EN>
All at once , he is taking on responsibility for the strategy of a bank that has once again proven that it has long deserved the title of &quot; Europe &apos;s biggest banking scandal . &quot; <EN>
UBS is both huge - it was the biggest asset manager in the world until recently - and has been struggling from one scandal to the next for years . <EN>
The proud Swiss bank , it seems , is to be spared nothing . <EN>
It began in the financial crisis . <EN>
UBS had an excellent reputation until 2007 . <EN>
The bank combined the image of the secretive and solid , but equally savvy asset manager with ambitious targets , aiming to become a major player in investment banking . <EN>
As a result , in 2007 UBS was managing 1.6 billion , thereby managing more more money from wealthy clients than any other bank in the world , <EN>
and had risen to the league of the world &apos;s biggest banks as an investment bank . <EN>
That made an impression . <EN>
The former banker and long-standing banking professor at the Swiss Institute of Banking of the University of Zurich , Hans Geiger , explains: &quot; I always presented UBS to my students as the model of a good bank . &quot; <EN>
&quot; From what we know today , you have to ask how I could be so wrong . &quot; <EN>
He was very wrong indeed . <EN>
It only became clear in 2007 that something was really going very wrong at UBS . <EN>
In the middle of the year , CEO Peter Wuffli - considered a highly intellectual and equally brilliant banker - suddenly stepped down . <EN>
Some months later we could guess at why he had left . <EN>
The investment division of the bank had gambled on subprime securities and was forced to write off billions . <EN>
UBS announced a capital increase , believe it or not , of 13 billion Swiss francs to face the crisis . <EN>
The bank actually managed to find investors , but investors many bankers would have respectfully declined a short while earlier - a less than transparent Asian sovereign wealth fund from Singapore and an Arabic sovereign wealth fund that was so secretive , even its name was not disclosed . <EN>
That was just the first blow . <EN>
It got a lot worse in April 2008 . <EN>
The bank was forced to announce new losses running into the billions and Chairman of the Board of Directors , Marcel Ospel - the second best paid chairman in Switzerland in 2006 - resigned . <EN>
Catastrophe followed in October 2008 . UBS faced collapse from a lack of investment during the financial crisis and had to be saved by the state . <EN>
The National Bank bought up toxic securities from UBS for untold billions and the Swiss Confederation paid six billion Swiss francs for a mandatory convertible bond to become part owner of the bank . <EN>
The whole of Switzerland was shocked - the country recognised the dramatic consequences for a small country of being home to such large banks . <EN>
After all , the balance sheet total for UBS in 2007 was more than five times the economic output of Switzerland (see chart). <EN>
&quot; We would not be able to save the UBS for a second time , &quot; says banking researcher Geiger . <EN>
The second catastrophe followed closely on the heels of the first . <EN>
A few months later , UBS capitulated in the tax dispute with the USA and declared that it was prepared to hand over the data of wealthy clients who had potentially avoided paying tax with the help of the bank . <EN>
UBS also agreed to pay 780 million dollars consisting of repayment of unjustified profits from the business and a penalty . <EN>
UBS therefore more or less admitted having been an accessory to tax evasion . <EN>
At the same time , UBS lost something that had always been its advantage when competing for rich clients - the fog of secrecy . <EN>
Swiss banking secrecy was not the same after the scandal . <EN>
The CEO and the Chairman then resigned and <EN>
the exodus of client money began . <EN>
The bank had lost its credibility in both of its core business divisions within a few months - in investment banking thanks to bad speculation and in asset management by aiding and abetting tax evasion . <EN>
And just as things had calmed down and UBS looked like it would start to turn things around , along came a disastrous rogue trader . A single trader gambled away 1.7 billion Euros before the bank noticed something was wrong . <EN>
One thing is clear - risk management in the investment banking division is still not working . <EN>
&quot; The Adoboli incident clearly showed that risk control had changed too little , &quot; says Martin Janssen , economic and professor of finance at the Swiss Banking Institute of the University of Zurich . <EN>
The CFO of one major German bank also has no doubts: &quot; The problem facing UBS is that it does not having a handle on risk control . &quot; <EN>
It was precisely the concept of caution that had long ago made Swiss bankers the guardians of the world &apos;s major assets - no excessive risk , but security for money , whether the world fell apart outside the Alpine republic or not . <EN>
The safes of Swiss banks had become a symbol of unshakeable reliability , just as Lindt and Sprüngli had come to symbolise sophisticated chocolate . <EN>
The UBS headquarters in Zurich still fit the cliché of the dignified Swiss private bank - just a bit bigger . <EN>
The location alone is classic . <EN>
The bank has its head office on Zurich &apos;s Bahnhofstrasse that leads from the main station directly to Zurich Lake , surrounded by the snow-capped peaks of the Swiss mountains . <EN>
The buildings are ostentatious and the shop rates are among the highest in Europe . <EN>
Jewellers such as Tiffany &apos;s are to be found here between traditional Swiss shops such as Confiserie Sprüngli . <EN>
The Swiss banks have resided here for hundreds of years - from the National Bank to the palace of Credit Suisse and elite private banks such as Julius Bär . <EN>
A heavy revolving door opens onto the UBS reception . <EN>
The walls within are clad in marble behind vast leather armchairs . There is a large sign to the &quot; Safe &quot; next to the bank &apos;s logo . <EN>
UBS knows that its clients are looking for - security . <EN>
But both the major Swiss banks , UBS and Credit Suisse , at some point ousted the Swiss banking concept - or betrayed it , as the head of one small Swiss private bank believes . <EN>
He would prefer not to see his name in the newspaper - he too , like all Swiss bankers , does business with the two major banks . <EN>
He believes UBS has grown too big - particularly in investment banking where the Anglo-Saxons are also very active . <EN>
In his opinion , the Swiss have nothing to add . <EN>
&quot; And if they do , they have adapted to the customs of the Anglo-Saxons long ago . &quot; <EN>
It was in fact Anglo-Saxon investment banking that changed UBS , brought in its first big profits - and then the debacle . No other European financial institution has lost as much money in the subprime jungle as the major Swiss bank . <EN>
The catastrophe became evident on 15 October 2008 . <EN>
&quot; That Wednesday , the government coalition of a small country with a population of seven million undertook the largest rescue operation in the history of the nation , &quot; writes author Lukas Hässig in his book The UBS Crash . <EN>
The politicians approved up to 68 billion Swiss francs (around 45 billion Euros) to save the bank from bankruptcy . <EN>
How could it have come to that ? <EN>
Talking to Swiss banks , they see the issue mainly in the size of UBS . <EN>
Two of the three major Swiss banks consolidated into a single , vast group in June 1998 . <EN>
A bank was created that was already too big for small Switzerland when the merger was agreed - and a bank that continued to grow . <EN>
The fact that the two banks that went to form UBS complemented each other helped . One was a wealthy but sedate bank specialising in asset management in Zurich and the other was less wealthy , but much more internationalised . <EN>
The internationalised investment bankers suddenly had access to a lot of money that they could use to turn an almighty wheel . <EN>
Two names are connected with the rise of UBS: Peter Wuffli , Group CEO of UBS from 2001 to 2007 , and Marcel Ospel , Chairman of the Board of Directors . <EN>
&quot; I always thought that Wuffli and Ospel were a dream team , &quot; says the banking research , Hans Geiger . <EN>
&quot; Wuffli , highly intellectual , modest , with a deep understanding of models and statistics , and Ospel , with gut instinct who had worked his way up from being a banker &apos;s apprentice . &quot; <EN>
But Ospel in the end relied on Wuffli . <EN>
And Wuffli ultimately may have made a critical error . &quot; He thought his models were reality , &quot; says Geiger . <EN>
&quot; That is tragic . &quot; <EN>
Tragic it may be . <EN>
Pride comes before a fall . <EN>
Employees of UBS clearly remember the management meetings where CEO Wuffli always repeated the same slogan - dethrone Goldman Sachs . <EN>
The American bank was the world &apos;s most powerful investment bank . <EN>
It led the &quot; league tables &quot; that documented the success of the banks at that time . <EN>
UBS wanted to get to the very top of the league . <EN>
It managed some of the way . <EN>
UBS was a major player in foreign exchange and stocks . <EN>
Commissioned management consultants , however , pointed out a weakness . In terms of what in banking terminology is referred to as &quot; fixed income , &quot; UBS was far behind the very largest banks . <EN>
UBS had gaps in its US mortgage products . <EN>
To plug the hole , UBS entered on an adventure that almost cost it its existence . <EN>
Hungry for growth , the bank itself and a hedge fund founded by the bank invested in US subprime securities . <EN>
It developed into a vast machine that packaged up securities based on US mortgage credit and passed them on - while itself continuing to bear risks . <EN>
Even when other banks had long been looking for a way out , UBS carried on . <EN>
&quot; UBS was buying as late as the summer of 2007 when the US housing market was in flames , &quot; says banking expert Geiger . <EN>
The greater the rise , the greater the fall . <EN>
One manager after the next had to go as the attempts to clean up proved more difficult than anticipated . <EN>
Posts at UBS became a game of musical chairs and remain uncertain to this day . <EN>
Any head of the major bank now has an almost impossible job . <EN>
He must find a strategy for a bank that has turned its back on all existing business models . <EN>
Banking expert Geiger already has an idea - quit investment banking , focus on asset management and turn back to Swiss roots . <EN>
The bank , however , is not (yet) prepared to go that far . <EN>
It is clear , nonetheless , that investment banking must shrink significantly . <EN>
The new head of the bank , Sergio Ermotti , plans to present his future strategy to the world on Tuesday . <EN>
The 51-year-old Italo-Swiss banker was actually only imagined as a transitional solution when the bank parted ways unexpectedly with his predecessor Grübel . <EN>
Since then , he has proved his mettle and is now to head UBS permanently , the Zurich-based bank announced on Tuesday . <EN>
Ermotti plans to take the investment bank back to where it was in the mid-90s . <EN>
He is cutting 3500 jobs . <EN>
But that will not be enough . <EN>
UBS needs a vision . <EN>
What is UBS ? <EN>
How does it plan to make money ? <EN>
Those are the questions Axel Weber is definitely already asking himself . <EN>
Publicly , he has only so far that he and his wife will look for a flat in Zurich . <EN>
Next year . <EN>
Fear of recession in Europe depresses US stock exchange <EN>
The impending recession in Europe has depressed the mood of US investors at the start of the week . <EN>
The change of government in Athens and Rome had little impact . <EN>
Curbed industrial production on the continent nipped hopes that the debt crisis might stabilise in the bud . <EN>
The general relief following the change of government in Rome and Athens was not sustained . <EN>
The Euro fell against the dollar . <EN>
The Italian and Greek glass was still considered half full last week , not half empty - now the problems are coming to the fore once again , said Mark Luschini of Janney Montgomery Scott . <EN>
Financial stocks in particular were on the sales receipts . <EN>
The Dow Jones Industrial Average closed business at 12,078 with a fall of 0.6 percent . <EN>
The market barometer fluctuated between 12,027 and 12,170 points in the course of trading . <EN>
The broader S &amp; P 500 index closed at 1251 point , down one percent . <EN>
The Nasdaq Technology Index lost 0.8 percent and closed trading at 2657 points . <EN>
In Frankfurt , the Dax fell 1.2 percent closing at 5985 points . <EN>
Industry in the 17 Euro countries has significantly reduced production and is adjusting to the end of the upturn . <EN>
The Eurostat statistics office announced that , in September , companies produced two percent less than in the previous month . <EN>
The announcement made US investors sceptical . &quot; We are not an island . We are dependent , &quot; said Steve Goldman of Goldman Management . <EN>
He also claimed that Europe is not likely to shake off a recession quickly and that there are further signs of weakness in the banks . <EN>
The investment legend , Warren Buffett , could only support such caution . In a CNBC interview , he said that it was not yet clear whether Europe is strong enough to do all that is needed to end the crisis . <EN>
In his opinion , it is therefore too early to invest in European government bonds or banks . <EN>
Instead , Buffett threw a decades-old principle out of the window to invest in the US technology industry . <EN>
His investment of more than ten billion dollars in IBM boosted the veteran company &apos;s share price by almost one percent against the trend during the course of trading . <EN>

The bank primarily plans to bolster its capital quota with the net profit from the sale to meet tougher regulations . <EN>

Intelligent crows are spreading in cities <EN>
Rooks are considered problem birds in many places . Experts now say the highly intelligent animals can no longer be driven from cities . <EN>
Some like the birds , others would like to get rid of them as fast as possible . Crows have been part of the cityscape for hundreds of years , but residents complaining about the filth and noise the animals create are increasing in number in many communities . <EN>
A solution to the problem birds , however , is far from within reach . <EN>
Experts at the first crow symposium in the East Frisian town of Leer have said that rooks can no longer be forced out of cities . <EN>
Specialists from all over Germany discussed possible solutions . <EN>
Looking for alternatives in the cities <EN>
Conservationists stated that migration of specially protected rooks was the root of the problem in cities , pointing out that the use of chemicals in agriculture was increasingly destroying traditional habitats . <EN>
Hunting , increasing development and felling of typical breeding trees was making life hard for the birds . <EN>
Crows are protected . <EN>
There are large colonies with more than 600 breeding pairs in the Westphalian town of Soest and in the north-west in Jever , Diepholz , Achim bei Bremen and Leer . <EN>
A controversial project to cull crows in Leer was behind negative headlines in 2005 . <EN>
Critics described the capture of the birds in bird traps and how they were beaten to death with clubs as particularly brutal . <EN>
&quot; Normal displacement and deterrence does nothing , &quot; said town and country planner Werner Klöver from Leer . <EN>
Spraying off nests with water or felling trees often has undesired consequences , said environment expert Manfred Kaiser from Lahr in Baden-Württemberg . <EN>
&quot; The animals disperse and large colonies split up and spread to other areas . &quot; <EN>
Deterrence would only be conceivable as an exception in hospitals , retirement homes and schools . <EN>
&quot; We have to live with them . Getting rid of them is not an option . &quot; <EN>
Without the surrounding area , the problem in the cities will not be solved , said Leer &apos;s mayor , Wolfgang Kellner . <EN>
A combination of deterring birds from sensitive residential areas and offering incentives for them to move back to other areas would be an option . <EN>
&quot; Information boards instead of chain saws &quot; was the slogan proposed by the psychologist and ethnologist Uta Maria Jürgens , who argued for a totally different approach to the birds . &quot; We should have the self-confidence to live with this problem . &quot; <EN>
Jürgens was a co-founder of the Ascherberg crow educational trail in Schleswig-Holstein , where notice boards provide information about the life of the highly intelligent rook . <EN>
The project is already attracting interest from tourists . <EN>
Jürgens also expressed her opinion on the criticism of the noise the birds make . &quot; The noise conveys a lot of information . They have a lot to say to each other . &quot; <EN>
The intelligence and skill of the birds are legendary . Rooks often do not just use tools to get hold of a choice morsel , but create tools themselves . <EN>
Behavioural researchers at the University of Cambridge recently tested the extent of the birds &quot; intelligence on four rooks . <EN>
In one experiment , the birds quickly learnt that they had to knock over a platform to get to a moth larva . <EN>
They recognised the size and shape of stone needed to collapse the platform without much training . <EN>
In a second experiment , the canny crows had to solve a trickier problem . <EN>
The researchers put a small bucket with a moth larva in a vertical cylinder . <EN>
The birds could not reach their prey with their beaks . <EN>
However , the researchers had provided pieces of wire . <EN>
All four birds used the wire to form a hook and used the hook to fish the bucket out of the tube by its handle . <EN>
Three of the four rooks even managed it at the first attempt . <EN>
Ronaldo rockets Portugal to Euro 2012 <EN>
The hopes of Bosnians and Turks for a last minute win were short-lived . <EN>
The favourites Portugal , Croatia and the Czech Republic , plus Ireland , will be at the 2012 European championship . <EN>

Mass Slaughter on a Personal Level <EN>
Peter Englund &apos;s intense and bighearted new book , &quot; The Beauty and the Sorrow: An Intimate History of the First World War , &quot; begins with a long dramatis personae of the sort that can make your heart sink . <EN>
Here is advice for proceeding: Gently excise this page and make it your bookmark . <EN>
You will be getting to know these people very well in Mr. Englund &apos;s novelistic telling , and this dramatis personae will function as your GPS , a beacon during those few moments when , like one of his men and women , you are confused and bereft in the fog of war . <EN>
Mr. Englund is a Swedish historian and journalist . <EN>
He is also the new permanent secretary of the Swedish Academy , which awards the Nobel Prize in Literature . <EN>
What he has written here is an unusual book , one he describes , not inaccurately , as &quot; a work of anti-history . &quot; <EN>
It contains few big names , major treaties or famous battles; there are almost no ambassadors , dashing journalists or discussions of tactics and materiel . <EN>
It &apos;s not so much a book about what happened , he explains , as &quot; a book about what it was like . &quot; It &apos;s about &quot; feelings , impressions , experiences and moods . &quot; <EN>
&quot; The Beauty and the Sorrow &quot; threads together the wartime experiences of 20 more or less unremarkable men and women , on both sides of the war , from schoolgirls and botanists to mountain climbers , doctors , ambulance drivers and clerks . <EN>
A few of these people will become heroes . <EN>
A few will become prisoners of war , or lose limbs , go mad or die . <EN>
Their lives flicker here like votive candles lighted in a church; new ones are added to the mix while some wink out . <EN>
Mr. Englund &apos;s book is a deviation from standard history books . <EN>
It is a corrective too to the notion that World War I was only about the dire trench warfare on the Western Front . <EN>
&quot; The Beauty and the Sorrow &quot; expertly pans across other theaters of war: the Alps , the Balkans , the Eastern Front , Mesopotamia , East Africa . <EN>
Soldiers in this book have beehives fall on them; one has Christmas in Egypt under the pyramids; tsetse flies are an intractable problem . <EN>
This is a moving book , almost from the start . <EN>
War floods these people &apos;s lives like a natural catastrophe , a Hurricane Katrina that reeks of cordite . <EN>
When cannon fire is heard in the distance , and you are a woman at home with your children , do you stay or flee ? <EN>
Who is coming , anyway ? <EN>
Almost no one understands what &apos;s happening , even why this war is to be fought . <EN>
&quot; Lack of facts , &quot; Mr. Englund observes , &quot; has been padded out with guesses , suppositions , hopes , fears , idées fixes , conspiracy theories , dreams , nightmares and rumors . &quot; <EN>
&quot; The Beauty and the Sorrow &quot; follows individuals like Florence Farmborough , an English nurse in the Russian Army , and Richard Stumpf , a young German high-seas fleet seaman . <EN>
Their stories are mostly taken from memoirs , letters and other already published material . <EN>
The accounts of their lives can be terrifying or stirring , but are most fully alive in Mr. Englund &apos;s accumulation of small moments , stray details . <EN>
Many of these are about deprivation and making do . <EN>
In telling a German schoolgirl &apos;s story he says: &quot; Ersatz , everywhere ersatz . &quot; <EN>
&quot; Substitute coffee , fake aluminum , imitation rubber , paper bandages , wooden buttons . &quot; <EN>
He goes on about the ersatz food in Germany . <EN>
He describes &quot; meat made of pressed rice boiled in mutton fat (and finished off with a fake bone made of wood); tobacco made of dried roots and dried potato peel; shoes soled with wood . &quot; <EN>
There are , he notes , &quot; 837 registered meat substitutes permissible in the production of sausages , 511 registered coffee substitutes . &quot; <EN>
Some stories are about honor and bravery . <EN>
One American recognizes his own impulse toward savagery and declares about war: &quot; You feel that , after all , this is what men were intended for rather than to sit in easy chairs with a cigarette and whiskey , the evening paper or the best seller , and to pretend that such a veneer means civilization and that there is no barbarian behind your starched and studded shirt front . &quot; <EN>
Conversely a British soldier realizes that he will most likely die , and that no one will notice or care . <EN>
&quot; Once one is resigned to the thought of sacrificing oneself , one would like to think that it might happen in front of an audience , &quot; he writes . <EN>
Instead , it is horribly like &quot; a condemned man being strangled secretly . &quot; <EN>
Other observations are about an old Europe falling away , and about new types of terror . <EN>
&quot; The conflict has increasingly become an economic competition , &quot; Mr. Englund writes , &quot; a war between factories . &quot; <EN>
He catches the arrival of what he calls &quot; a new species in the bestiary of the young century: the articulate and ideologically convinced mass murderer in well-cut clothes who performs his butchery while sitting behind a desk . &quot; <EN>
People behave in unanticipated ways; there is as much base behavior as heroism . <EN>
Mr. Englund discussed the soldiers who actively tried to catch a venereal disease from prostitutes as a way to evade service at the front . <EN>
&quot; The most grotesque expression of this can be seen in the trade of gonococcal pus , which soldiers buy and smear into their genitals in the hope of ending up in hospital , &quot; he writes . <EN>
&quot; Those who are really desperate rub it into their eyes , which often results in lifelong blindness . &quot; <EN>
In this translation from the Swedish by Peter Graves , Mr. Englund &apos;s prose is supple but unshowy , perfectly suited to his humane task . <EN>
In dozens of small scenes he catches the way the war has &quot; unleashed uniquely uncontrollable forces: extreme nationalism , social revolution , religious hatred . &quot; <EN>
People begin to ask why their leaders are making them fight . <EN>
The best books about World War I have often been oblique , like Paul Fussell &apos;s &quot; Great War and Modern Memory , &quot; or novels , like Erich Maria Remarque &apos;s &quot; All Quiet on the Western Front , &quot; rather than comprehensive histories . <EN>
Mr. Englund &apos;s volume joins an unconventional pantheon . <EN>
His book has the most devastating ending I can remember in a piece of nonfiction . <EN>
I won &apos;t give it away . <EN>
But it &apos;s as if he has reached from his book , snatched that dramatis personae page from your fingers , and lighted it with a match . <EN>
After an Earlier Misstep , a Minutely Planned Raid <EN>
Hundreds of police officers were involved , some of them wearing riot helmets . <EN>
The overnight hours of Monday into Tuesday were chosen because Zuccotti Park would be at its emptiest . <EN>
The operation was kept secret from all but a few high-ranking officers , with others initially being told that they were embarking on an exercise . <EN>
Police Commissioner Raymond W. Kelly was at the center , his presence underscoring how the operation was fraught with challenges for the Police Department . <EN>
There could be no repeat of episodes in recent weeks , like the pepper-spraying of protesters , that violated department rules and created a firestorm of public sympathy for the squatters . <EN>
And so the police operation to clear Zuccotti Park of protesters unfolded after two weeks of planning and training . <EN>
Officials had prepared by watching how occupations in other cities played out . <EN>
A major disaster drill was held on Randalls Island , with an eye toward Zuccotti . <EN>
Officials increased so-called disorder training - counterterrorism measures that involve moving large numbers of police officers quickly - to focus on Lower Manhattan . <EN>
The last training session was on Monday night , on the Manhattan side of the East River . <EN>
The orders to move into the park came down at the &quot; last minute , &quot; said someone familiar with the orders , which referred to the assignment only as &quot; an exercise . &quot; <EN>
&quot; The few cops that I know that were called into this thing , they were not told it was for going into Zuccotti Park , &quot; said the person , who spoke on the condition of anonymity . <EN>
&quot; The only people who were aware of them going into Zuccotti Park were at the very highest levels of the department . &quot; <EN>
One reason for the secrecy was a lesson learned by the city . <EN>
On Oct. 14 , officials wanted to clear the park , but then backed off as hundreds of protesters streamed in ahead of time after hearing of the plans . <EN>
The operation on Tuesday involved officers from various police units , including boroughwide task forces - scores of mobile officers who are usually used to flood high-crime neighborhoods . <EN>
Mr. Kelly said many people , almost like commuters , had been coming and going from the park during the day , making 1 a.m. a good time to move in . <EN>
&quot; It was appropriate to do it when the smallest number of people were in the park , &quot; he said . <EN>
Emergency Service Unit trucks with klieg lights and loudspeakers gathered at Pike Slip and the Franklin D. Roosevelt Drive , near the Manhattan Bridge , before moving out . <EN>
The lights and prerecorded messages booming from the loudspeakers seemed to cow many protesters . <EN>
As the community affairs officers moved into the park in their light-blue windbreakers , many protesters simply gathered their belongings and left . <EN>
No tents were touched until 1: 45 a.m. , the police said , giving the protesters time to gather their belongings . <EN>
Other teams of officers were seen gathering on the perimeter to move in if arrests were needed in the park . <EN>
Reporters in the park were forced to leave . <EN>
Paul J. Browne , the Police Department &apos;s chief spokesman , said it was for their safety . <EN>
But many journalists said that they had been prevented from seeing the police take action in the park , and that they had been roughly handled by officers . <EN>
Mr. Browne said television camera trucks on Church Street , along the park &apos;s western border , were able to capture images . <EN>
As the police moved west through the dense tangle of protesters &quot; personal belongings , including luggage and plastic lawn and leaf bags stuffed with clothing , crews from the Sanitation Department followed , scooping up what was left behind . <EN>
Some protesters who refused to move were dragged out , the images appearing on the Internet soon after . <EN>
A core group of protesters took up positions close to the encampment &apos;s kitchen area , near the center of the park . <EN>
Some made a barrier , and the police moved in to methodically arrest them . <EN>
About 10 people in the epicenter of the encampment locked themselves together by their arms . <EN>
And two people chained themselves to trees , Mr. Kelly said . <EN>
Emergency service officers were called in to cut the locks . <EN>
No arrests were made in the park until about 3: 30 a.m. , Mr. Kelly said . <EN>
The clearing operation was complete about 75 minutes later , the police said . <EN>
Mr. Browne said about 142 people were arrested in the park . <EN>
Most of the arrests were for &quot; disorderly conduct and resisting arrest , &quot; he said . <EN>
The highest-ranking officer on the scene was Joseph J. Esposito , the chief of department , the top uniformed officer in the department . <EN>
Phil T. Pulaski , the department &apos;s chief of detectives , was also there . <EN>
Mr. Kelly , while present , was &quot; not directing operations , &quot; Mr. Browne said . <EN>
A second group of officers waited along the eastern side of Broadway , between Liberty and Cedar Streets , in case they had to move in . <EN>
Barricades were set up at Cortlandt Street , a block north of the park , and at Pine Street , a block south . <EN>
From those positions , the police were seen expanding the perimeter even farther outward from Zuccotti Park . <EN>
At one point , several officers , many with shields , were seen pushing people farther out . <EN>
About 28 people were on the northern perimeter . <EN>
Some of the rowdiest action of the night took place south of the park . <EN>
Around 5 a.m. , south of Pine Street , one protester jumped on the hood of a police car , and others were seen releasing the air from the tires of a police van . <EN>
At one point , a piece of plywood came flying from the crowd . <EN>
In the end , one officer and one protester were hospitalized . <EN>
Support Workers &apos; Union Will Sue City Over Layoffs <EN>
The union representing hundreds of school support workers who lost their jobs last month plans to sue the city on Wednesday , claiming the layoffs were unnecessary and discriminatory because of their disproportionate impact on schools that serve poor students . <EN>
The lawsuit is possibly the last weapon available to the union , District Council 37 , in its effort to reverse the layoffs . <EN>
Six hundred seventy-two school aides , parent coordinators and other employees who were among the city &apos;s lowest paid lost their jobs on Oct. 7 , in a move union leaders have described as political payback for their refusal to let the city access a health care fund run by labor groups to close its budget gap last spring . <EN>
City officials have categorically denied that accusation . <EN>
At a City Council hearing last month , Schools Chancellor Dennis M. Walcott said the layoffs were a part of the budget they signed off on in June . <EN>
One council member fired back , telling him that nothing in the budget specified that school support staff members would be laid off . <EN>
District Council 37 officials said they filed a notice of claim , warning the Department of Education that it would be sued; it will hold a news conference on Wednesday to announce the lawsuit &apos;s filing formally , in State Supreme Court in Manhattan . <EN>
The suit will list Mr. Walcott and the city &apos;s Department of Education as defendants , and counts eight laid-off workers as plaintiffs , all of them black or Latino women , as were most of the aides who lost their jobs . <EN>
Elizabeth Thomas , a spokeswoman for the city &apos;s Law Department , said the city had not seen the lawsuit and therefore could not comment on its specific allegations . <EN>
According to a draft of the complaint obtained by The New York Times , the union has zeroed in on the number of layoffs at schools in poor parts of the city to support a claim of inequitable treatment , saying poor schools lost more aides because they had been chronically underfinanced . <EN>
It points out that while there were no layoffs on Staten Island and few layoffs in schools in the Upper East Side or TriBeCa , 17 school aides lost their jobs in District 23 in Brownsville , Brooklyn , and 46 were let go in Districts 8 and 9 in the South Bronx . <EN>
Noting the loss of five out of eight school aides employed by Public School 36 in Harlem , where 68 percent of the students live in poverty , the lawsuit says , &quot; This is not a neighborhood of well-heeled parents who can fund-raise to make up the budget shortfalls . &quot; <EN>
P.S. 36 &quot; s budget was cut by 3.26 percent this year , and it also lost money when the city changed the way it calculates the extra financing for each poor student schools enroll . <EN>
The union also claims that high school principals may have been misled by the language in a memo authorizing the dismissal of parent coordinators . <EN>
The memo used the word &quot; excess &quot; to describe the action , even though &quot; excess &quot; more commonly describes the act of moving a teacher from a school &apos;s payroll into a pool of available workers whose salaries are paid by the central office . <EN>
&quot; Sixty-six parent coordinators were laid off , &quot; the draft complaint says , &quot; and not merely excessed . &quot; <EN>
Mission over , Congress ready to agree on Libya <EN>
It finally looks like Republicans and Democrats on Capitol Hill are ready to agree on something related to the uprising in Libya . <EN>
All it took was for the revolt to succeed , longtime dictator Moammar Gaddafi to be captured and killed and American involvement to end . <EN>
On Tuesday , the Senate Foreign Relations Committee is to consider a resolution , sponsored by Chairman John Kerry (D-Mass .), along with Sens. John McCain (R-Ariz .) and Joseph I. Lieberman (I-Conn .), applauding Libyans for their successful rebellion and U.S. troops for their &quot; bravery . &quot; <EN>
&quot; This resolution is about honoring the courageous people of Libya as they begin to rebuild their country , &quot; Kerry said . <EN>
&quot; It &apos;s an affirmation of bipartisan support for their democratic aspirations . &quot; <EN>
The language may sound innocuous , but nothing about the Libya debate has been easy so far . <EN>
This summer , lawmakers from both parties squabbled with each other and the White House over the wording of a series of resolutions to approve or disapprove of the U.S. military &apos;s role in the NATO mission in Libya . <EN>
In June , Kerry and McCain introduced a resolution authorizing the limited use of U.S. military forces in Libya . <EN>
The bill was defeated in the House by a wide bipartisan margin , and it never came up for a vote in the Senate . <EN>
But on the same day that bill failed in the House , the chamber also voted down a measure that would have cut funding for American operations in Libya . <EN>
That left the U.S. mission in a form of legislative purgatory - with Congress upset enough to criticize Obama &apos;s handling of the mission but not so angry as to actually pull the rug out from under it . <EN>
Then Congress &apos;s indecision was overtaken by events . <EN>
Tripoli fell to Libyan rebels in August , and Gaddafi was killed Oct. 20 . <EN>
The NATO mission officially ended Oct. 31 . <EN>
Now the Senate may be ready to act . <EN>
The Foreign Relations Committee resolution &quot; congratulates the people of Libya for their tremendous courage and extraordinary resilience in liberating themselves &quot; and &quot; commends the men and women of the United States Armed Forces and their coalition partners who engaged in military operations to protect the people of Libya for their extraordinary bravery and professionalism . &quot; <EN>
The resolution also &quot; affirms the national interest of the United States in a successful and irreversible transition to democracy in Libya . &quot; <EN>
Will the new measure earn the full support of the Foreign Relations panel , or will it split lawmakers like the June bill did ? <EN>
The last version was opposed by Sen. Richard G. Lugar (Ind .), the committee &apos;s top Republican . <EN>
Lugar &apos;s spokesman said Monday that he had not seen the final version of the new bill yet . <EN>
Across the Capitol , the House is to vote this week on a constitutional amendment requiring a balanced budget , a top legislative priority of nearly every congressional Republican and some Democrats . <EN>
The measure , sponsored by Rep. Bob Goodlatte (R-Va .), will be the first constitutional amendment on the budget or any other topic to actually get a floor vote in the House or Senate this Congress . <EN>
Other lawmakers have been unsuccessful so far in bringing their amendments to the floor , but not for lack of trying . <EN>
Goodlatte &apos;s is just one of 68 constitutional amendments that have been introduced this Congress , spanning a wide range of topics . <EN>
Some are duplicates - the same bill offered in both the House and Senate - and others are slight variations on each other . <EN>
There are at least 15 versions of the balanced budget amendment in the House alone , and another handful that would &quot; control federal spending . &quot; <EN>
Some of those bills are identical too , but they give their sponsors - particularly freshmen Republicans looking to burnish their resumes - the chance to brag that they &quot; authored &quot; such a measure . <EN>
The Budget Control Act , which passed in August , required that both the House and Senate vote on a balanced budget amendment . <EN>
In March , 58 senators voted in favor of a non-binding resolution supporting the idea of such an amendment . <EN>
Beyond the budget , several members want to limit the number of terms members of Congress can serve , while Rep. José E. Serrano (D-N.Y.) wants to lift the two-term limit for presidents . <EN>
Rep. Jesse L. Jackson Jr . (D-Ill .) has offered a host of amendments guaranteeing the right to quality education and health care , among other subjects . <EN>
An amendment prohibiting same-sex marriage is a perennial offering , as is one prohibiting flag-burning . <EN>
Some lawmakers also want to allow for the nullification of federal laws if they are opposed by two-thirds of the states . <EN>
As eager as members have been to offer amendments , they &apos;re not moving at any faster pace than in past years . <EN>
In the 111th Congress , lawmakers offered 77 such amendments , and they introduced 66 in the 110th . <EN>
The pace pales in comparison to that of the early 1990s , when members regularly offered more than 150 amendments every two years , according to numbers provided by the Senate Library . <EN>
But they weren &apos;t much more successful then than they are now . <EN>
The last amendment to be added - the 27th - was ratified in 1992 , but it was actually proposed by Congress in 1789 . <EN>

Ten months after a gunman shot her at point-blank range at a constituent event in Tucson , Rep. Three months ago , she made a surprise return to the House to triumphantly cast her vote on the debt-ceiling deal . <EN>

A pucker of the lips . <EN>

Within days , Giffords uttered another word - &quot; toast , &quot; a request for a change in her breakfast menu . <EN>

You &apos;ve just been beat up . <EN>
